## 🇸🇪 Sweden

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Be exactly on time — Swedish punctuality is structural and taken seriously
- Use first names from first contact, including with senior figures
- Take *fika* (the coffee-and-cake break) at 10:00 and 15:00; it is genuinely sacred
- Toast with eye contact on every *skål*, looking at each person around the table
- Remove your shoes when entering any private home

**Avoid**
- Boasting; *Jantelagen* (the Law of Jante) is real and observed
- Loud or theatrical behaviour, especially in restaurants and public transport
- Confusing Sweden with Norway, Denmark, or Finland — the distinctions are felt
- Bringing up royal-family gossip casually — there is genuine affection for the institution
- Disagreement at meetings without consensus-building first; Swedish business decisions emerge from group quiet

### Core Value
*Lagom* — "just enough", the principle of balanced moderation that runs through Swedish design, business, and social life.

### Biggest Taboo
Visible status display, loud confidence, and self-promotion — all violate *Jantelagen*. Wealth in Sweden is real but understated; large cars, designer logos, and aggressive ambition read as bad form.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
*Fika* twice daily is structural. Lunch is light. Dinner is early at home (17:00–19:00). The classic toasting protocol (*skål*) requires eye contact with each person individually, before and after the sip. The host opens the meal.

**💬 Language Notes**
Swedish is North Germanic; English is universal and fluent. *Tack* (thank you) and *hej* (hi) are universal. Swedes appreciate effort but switch to English instantly to spare you difficulty.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wine, flowers (odd numbers, no chrysanthemums), or quality chocolate. Open at once with restrained appreciation. The host's children should be remembered with a small token.

**👔 Dress Code**
Quietly excellent, restrained, frequently black. Swedish business dresses below international norms but with very high quality. The *Filippa K* / *Acne Studios* aesthetic is the canonical look.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 50%
- **Voice Expression**: 18%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 32%

### Origin & Chronicle
Sweden was a great power in the seventeenth century, controlling much of the Baltic, before Charles XII's defeats reduced it to a Scandinavian kingdom. Two hundred years of unbroken peace since 1814 — including neutrality through both world wars — produced a country with rare social cohesion, the *folkhemmet* (people's home) welfare model, and a design culture (Bruno Mathsson, IKEA, Volvo, H&M) built on egalitarian functionalism. The cultural quiet, the love of the natural archipelago, and the political neutrality are continuous threads.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **GLASS · ✦ KOSTA BODA** — *Kosta Boda / Orrefors, Stockholm flagship*
   The 1742 Småland glassworks — Swedish art glass, the original *Pippi* range, and the country's heritage glass tradition.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A signed art-glass piece is the canonical Swedish corporate gift.

2. **DESIGN · ✦ SVENSKT TENN** — *Svenskt Tenn, Stockholm*
   The 1924 Stockholm interiors house — Josef Frank's botanical prints, the original Swedish Modern, the working canon.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Frank prints are licensed exclusively to Svenskt Tenn; reproductions elsewhere are unauthorised.

3. **FASHION · ✦ ACNE STUDIOS** — *Acne Studios Flagship, Stockholm*
   The 1996 Stockholm fashion house — the Swedish minimalist aesthetic at its established level, denim and outerwear especially.
   *Tags: Business · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The Norrmalmstorg flagship holds limited-edition pieces not exported.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦✦** — *Frantzén, Stockholm*
   Björn Frantzén's three-Michelin-star room in a Klara townhouse — Sweden's only three-star, with a Japanese-trained Nordic kitchen.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Booking opens months ahead; the chef's counter is the format to request.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦** — *Operakällaren, Stockholm*
   The Royal Opera House restaurant since 1787 — Stockholm's grand institution, with the matching gilt and Strindberg's old corner.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The classical Swedish menu (*kalops*, herring, smörgåsbord) is the heritage option.

3. **CAFÉ · ✦ FIKA INSTITUTION** — *Vete-Katten, Stockholm*
   Open since 1928 — the most architecturally intact Stockholm *konditori*, the proper *fika* with princess cake and *kanelbullar*.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Order *kanelbulle* and a coffee; both are unlimited refills in the *fika* tradition.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **MUSEUM · ✦ VASA** — *Vasamuseet, Stockholm*
   The 1628 warship raised from the harbour in 1961 — the world's only intact seventeenth-century ship, a Swedish architectural pilgrimage.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The first hour after opening is materially quieter than mid-day.

2. **OPERA · ✦ ROYAL** — *Kungliga Operan, Stockholm*
   The Royal Swedish Opera in its 1898 building on Gustav Adolfs torg — the country's serious music institution, with strong Nordic repertoire.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Drottningholm Court Theatre (summer) is the rococo-original venue, baroque and authentic.

3. **ARCHIPELAGO · ✦ CRUISE** — *Stockholm Archipelago, Stockholm*
   The 30,000 islands east of Stockholm — Waxholmsbolaget public ferries to Sandhamn, Vaxholm, and Grinda are the canonical Swedish day.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Sandhamn is the social island; Grinda is quieter and more dignified.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ NOBEL** — *Grand Hôtel Stockholm*
   On the harbour opposite the Royal Palace since 1874 — the official Nobel Prize hotel and the city's grand institution.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Mathias Dahlgren restaurant is the in-house heritage; the suites face the palace.

2. **DESIGN HOTEL · ✦ ARCHIPELAGO** — *Ett Hem, Stockholm*
   A 1910 Arts and Crafts townhouse in Östermalm — twenty-four rooms, the dignified residential alternative to the grand hotel.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The kitchen and library are residents-only and the social heart of the house.

3. **REMOTE LODGE · ✦ LAPLAND** — *Treehotel / ICEHOTEL, Swedish Lapland*
   The architectural treehouses at Harads and the original ICEHOTEL at Jukkasjärvi — the most ambitious northern-lights itinerary.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: ICEHOTEL is winter-only (December–April); the warm rooms are the dignified booking.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ NORDIC** — *European Flight Service / Sundt Air Sweden, Stockholm*
   The Stockholm-based business aviation — Globals and Falcons across the Nordic and Baltic regions.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Bromma airport (city) handles smaller jets; Arlanda is for ranges to North America.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ DIPLOMATIC** — *Cabonline Premium / Stockholm Limousines*
   The Mercedes service for the embassy and royal-court districts — bilingual, well-established.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Service is included; rounding up is the form, larger tips are awkward.

3. **CRUISE · ✦ ARCHIPELAGO PRIVATE** — *Stromma Premium / private yacht charter, Stockholm*
   The crewed-launch charters across the archipelago — the only serious way to see the islands.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Sandhamn–Stockholm sunset return is the classical Swedish summer evening.

## 🇷🇺 Russia

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Use patronymic (first name + father's name) with anyone older or more senior — *Ivan Petrovich*, *Maria Sergeevna*
- Bring an odd number of flowers to a host (even numbers are funeral)
- Toast at any meal with vodka or wine, looking at the person across from you
- Remove your shoes when entering any private home
- Take tea seriously — it is the universal social fluid, served at any time and any house

**Avoid**
- Refusing the first toast at a meal — refusal is a serious slight to the host
- Smiling at strangers in public — Russians read public smiles as insincere or unbalanced
- Whistling indoors (folk superstition: it makes money fly out of the house)
- Discussing politics with people you have just met, especially across foreign-Russian lines
- Confusing Russian culture with Soviet history; Russians distinguish the two carefully

### Core Value
*Dusha* — soul. Russians prize emotional depth, intellectual seriousness, and the long meal that becomes a long conversation that becomes a friendship.

### Biggest Taboo
Treating Russia as one of many post-Soviet countries. Russian self-conception is as the centre — culturally, politically, linguistically — of a vast Eurasian space, and the position is held seriously regardless of foreign opinion.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
The main meal is dinner, often long, with multiple toasts and *zakuski* (small appetisers) in waves. Vodka is taken in shots, never sipped, always with food. Bread is taken from a common basket. The host pours.

**💬 Language Notes**
Russian uses Cyrillic and is the only Slavic language with a global presence. *Spasibo* (thank you), *pozhaluysta* (please), and *zdravstvuyte* (formal hello) earn real credit. English is increasingly common among younger urban Russians; less so among older or rural.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Bring an odd number of flowers, good chocolate, or quality alcohol. Open immediately with thanks. Children of the host should be remembered and warmly greeted.

**👔 Dress Code**
Formal, well-tailored, dressier than international norms suggest. Moscow is one of the most fashion-conscious capitals; the Bolshoi requires evening wear; business expects dark suits.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 47%
- **Voice Expression**: 28%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 25%

### Origin & Chronicle
Russian identity was forged at the medieval crossroads of Byzantine Christianity (988), the Mongol yoke (1240–1480), and the Muscovite consolidation that became an empire under Peter and Catherine. The nineteenth-century literary revolution (Pushkin, Tolstoy, Dostoyevsky, Chekhov), the 1917 revolution, the seventy-four years of Soviet rule, the 1991 collapse, and the post-2000 reassertion have produced a culture of immense pride, philosophical seriousness, deep suspicion of outside narratives, and extraordinary depth in literature, music, ballet, and chess.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **PORCELAIN · ✦ IMPERIAL** — *Imperial Porcelain Factory, St. Petersburg*
   The 1744 manufactory of the Romanov court — hand-painted, with the *Cobalt Net* pattern that became the Soviet souvenir and the Russian heritage.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A signed Imperial cup is the canonical Russian state gift.

2. **AMBER · ✦ KALININGRAD** — *Russian Amber House, Moscow & St. Petersburg*
   The Baltic-coast amber houses — certified Russian amber, in classical and modern designs.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Look for the certified-amber stamp; tourist amber is often plastic.

3. **VODKA · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Russian Standard / Beluga / Imperia, premium retailers*
   The Russian heritage vodka houses — *Beluga Gold Line*, *Imperia*, the dignified Russian gift.
   *Tags: Business · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: A bottle of *Beluga Gold Line* is the canonical Russian corporate gift abroad.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦** — *Twins Garden, Moscow*
   The Berezutsky brothers' eco-conscious room — the country's first Michelin star, with a serious Russian-ingredients programme.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full Russian-Re-Invention tasting traces the country's culinary century.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MOSCOW INSTITUTION** — *Café Pushkin, Moscow*
   The faux-1820s aristocratic mansion on Tverskoy Boulevard — Russian *grande cuisine* in the imperial-era setting, open 24 hours.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Library room (formal) is the dignified booking; the Café room (informal) is for late-night.

3. **TEA HOUSE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Eliseyevsky / Eliseev Emporium, St. Petersburg*
   The 1903 Art Nouveau food hall on Nevsky Prospekt — the city's heritage caviar-and-tea institution, recently restored.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The chocolate counter holds *Krasnyi Oktyabr*, the imperial-era confection.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **BALLET · ✦ MARIINSKY** — *Mariinsky Theatre, St. Petersburg*
   The 1860 imperial ballet and opera house — the home of *Swan Lake*, *Sleeping Beauty*, and the world's foremost Russian-classical company.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The historic stage (Mariinsky I) is the architectural pilgrimage; Mariinsky II is the modern.

2. **BALLET · ✦ BOLSHOI** — *Bolshoi Theatre, Moscow*
   The 1825 imperial ballet on Theatre Square — the country's most prestigious house, with the Russian-distinctive Yuri Grigorovich repertoire.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Box seats are the heritage option; the parterre is acoustically best for opera.

3. **MUSEUM · ✦ HERMITAGE** — *State Hermitage Museum, St. Petersburg*
   The Winter Palace and the world's largest art collection — three million works in the imperial residence on the Neva.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Pre-book the Treasure Galleries (Gold Room and Diamond Room); access is timed and limited.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ IMPERIAL** — *Hotel Astoria, St. Petersburg*
   On St. Isaac's Square since 1912 — the city's grand institution, the address of state visits, recently restored to imperial-era specification.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The cathedral-view rooms over the square are requested specifically.

2. **PALACE HOTEL · ✦ MOSCOW** — *Four Seasons Hotel Moscow*
   On Manezhnaya Square in the original 1930s Hotel Moskva building — the most architecturally significant address in central Moscow, opposite the Kremlin.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Kremlin-view suites are limited; the rooftop bar is the city's serious view.

3. **CITY HOTEL · ✦ NEVSKY** — *Belmond Grand Hotel Europe, St. Petersburg*
   On Nevsky Prospekt since 1875 — the city's classical grand hotel, with the *L'Europe* dining room and the Russian heritage.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The historic Lidval suites are the architectural bookings.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ EURASIAN** — *Sirius-Aero / RusJet, Moscow*
   The Moscow-based business aviation operators — Globals and 737 BBJs across Eurasia (note: international sanctions affect operations).
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Vnukovo-3 is the dedicated business aviation terminal; Sheremetyevo is the airline.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ DIPLOMATIC** — *Mosgortrans Premium / private operators, Moscow & St. Petersburg*
   The Mercedes S-Class service — bilingual, well-established for the embassy and Kremlin districts.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Tipping ten percent is the form, in addition to fare.

3. **RAIL · ✦ SAPSAN** — *RZD Sapsan Business Class, Moscow–St. Petersburg*
   The Russian Railways high-speed business compartments — four hours, Moscow centre to St. Petersburg centre.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Sapsan business class is the dignified domestic alternative; the Red Arrow night train is the heritage option.

## 🇹🇷 Türkiye (Turkey)

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet older people with respect — kiss the back of an elder's hand and bring it to your forehead is the traditional gesture
- Accept tea (*çay*) whenever offered — it is the universal Turkish hospitality signal, refusing is rude
- Remove your shoes before entering any private home, and most religious sites
- Use the country name *Türkiye* (since the 2022 official re-naming); *Turkey* still acceptable in English casual
- Recognise that Turkish hospitality (*misafirperverlik*) is a serious obligation — the guest is sacred

**Avoid**
- Confusing Turkish identity with Arab — Turks are not Arabs, the language is unrelated, and the distinction is held
- Discussing the Armenian question, the Kurdish question, or the 1923 population exchange casually
- Smoking inside a mosque, or wearing shoes, or visible affection between unrelated men and women
- Pointing the soles of your feet at anyone (especially in a mosque or seated cross-legged)
- Insisting on paying when you are a guest — the Turkish host will fight you and that is the form

### Core Value
*Misafirperverlik* — the sacred hospitality. The guest is treated as a gift from God, and the host's obligation runs deep beyond what Western expectations suggest.

### Biggest Taboo
Treating Turkey as the Arab world or as Eastern Europe. Turkish identity is its own — Anatolian, Ottoman, modern Republican — and conflating it with neighbouring identities reads as ignorant and dismissive.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Turkish meals are long, plural, and shared. *Meze* opens the meal in waves. Bread is taken by hand from a common basket. The host insists on serving guests first and refilling glasses constantly. Coffee or tea closes the meal.

**💬 Language Notes**
Turkish is Turkic, written in Latin script since 1928, and unrelated to Arabic or Persian despite borrowed vocabulary. *Merhaba* (hello), *teşekkür ederim* (thank you), and *afiyet olsun* (bon appétit) earn credit. English is good in Istanbul tourism areas; less so elsewhere.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Quality chocolate, baklava from a recognised maker, or wine (where alcohol is welcome). Open at once with formal thanks. Bring something for the children of the host always.

**👔 Dress Code**
Conservative, well-tailored, more formal than European norms. Istanbul business is dressed for the meeting and the meal that follows. Mosque visits require shoulders and knees covered for everyone, and headscarves for women.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 42%
- **Voice Expression**: 30%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 28%

### Origin & Chronicle
The modern Turkish Republic was founded in 1923 by Atatürk on the ruins of the Ottoman Empire — itself a 600-year multi-ethnic state stretching from Vienna to Yemen. The Republican project (Latin script, secular state, women's suffrage in 1934) sits in productive tension with the deeper Anatolian and Ottoman inheritances. Istanbul is the only city in the world on two continents and has been Byzantine, Ottoman, and Turkish capital — fifteen hundred years of imperial culture is the bedrock of the country's pride.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **CARPETS · ✦ ANATOLIAN HERITAGE** — *Şişko Osman, Grand Bazaar, Istanbul*
   The fourth-generation rug house in the Cevahir Bedesten — the Istanbul authority on Anatolian, Caucasian, and Persian carpets.
   *Tags: Business · Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Tea is offered before the rugs are unrolled; the negotiation is part of the experience.

2. **JEWELLERY · ✦ ZULFARIS / GRAND BAZAAR** — *Sevan Bıçakçı, Istanbul*
   The Istanbul atelier of Sevan Bıçakçı — the only Turkish jeweller of international standing, with the *intaglio* technique he revived.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The atelier is by appointment; the showroom is in the historic peninsula.

3. **TILE · ✦ İZNİK CERAMICS** — *İznik Foundation, Istanbul & İznik*
   The 1993 foundation reviving authentic *İznik* tile — the original technique of the Suleymaniye and Topkapı tiles.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Authentic *İznik* is fired at very high temperatures; commercial *Kütahya* is the lower-cost alternative.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦** — *Turk Fatih Tutak, Istanbul*
   Fatih Tutak's two-Michelin-star room in Bomonti — the country's most ambitious modern Turkish kitchen, the only Turk-cuisine two-star in the world.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full menu traces the Anatolian regions; do the wine pairing for the rare Turkish bottles.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦** — *Mikla, Istanbul*
   Mehmet Gürs's rooftop room atop the Marmara Pera — the Bosphorus view with Anatolian-meets-Nordic cooking.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The terrace booking is for sunset; the inside dining for after.

3. **MEYHANE · ✦ ISTANBUL INSTITUTION** — *Asmalı Cavit, Istanbul*
   The Beyoğlu *meyhane* of the Istanbul intellectual class — *meze*, *rakı*, and the centuries-old Turkish-tavern tradition.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Order *rakı* with water and ice in three glasses; the *meze* arrive in waves.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **MOSQUE · ✦ OTTOMAN MASTERPIECE** — *Süleymaniye Mosque, Istanbul*
   Mimar Sinan's 1557 imperial mosque — the architectural peak of Ottoman religious building, less crowded than the Blue Mosque.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Avoid prayer hours; cover shoulders and knees; women cover hair.

2. **MUSEUM · ✦ TOPKAPI** — *Topkapı Palace Museum, Istanbul*
   The Ottoman court for four centuries — the imperial harem, the relics of the Prophet, and the world's most important Ottoman collection.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Pre-book the Harem (separate ticket); allow a full half-day for the complex.

3. **HAMAM · ✦ HERITAGE BATH** — *Çağaloğlu Hamamı / Çemberlitaş Hamamı, Istanbul*
   The 1741 and 1584 imperial Turkish baths — the dignified hamam experience, with the original marble *göbektaşı* (heated stone).
   *Tags: Friendly · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full *kese-and-massage* package is the protocol; do not rush it.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **PALACE HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Çırağan Palace Kempinski, Istanbul*
   The 1874 Ottoman palace on the Bosphorus — the only sultanic palace converted to a hotel, with the imperial-quay views.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Bosphorus-suite category is the architectural booking; the original palace rooms are limited.

2. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ ORIENT EXPRESS** — *Pera Palace Hotel, Istanbul*
   The 1892 hotel built for the Orient Express — Agatha Christie's room and the dignified Beyoğlu-side address.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Christie's room (411) is bookable but heavily reserved; the Greek-revival library is universal.

3. **BOUTIQUE · ✦ BOSPHORUS** — *Six Senses Kocataş Mansions, Istanbul*
   The Ottoman waterside *yali* mansions on the Bosphorus — the most refined modern luxury option in the city.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Bosphorus-side rooms are the architectural request; the boat-transfer to the city is part of the protocol.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ISTANBUL** — *MNG Jet / Borajet, Istanbul*
   The Istanbul-based business aviation operators — Globals and Challengers across Europe, the Middle East, and Central Asia.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Atatürk Airport (the old IST) handles dedicated business aviation; the new Istanbul Airport is for airline.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ BOSPHORUS** — *Trans-Travel / private operators, Istanbul*
   The Mercedes S-Class service — bilingual, well-established for the diplomatic and business districts.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Bosphorus traffic is severe; ferry on the Bosphorus is sometimes faster than road.

3. **PRIVATE BOAT · ✦ BOSPHORUS** — *Bosphorus Tour Premium / private *yali* charters, Istanbul*
   The classic teak-and-mahogany Bosphorus launches — the dignified way to take the strait.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Sunset between Anadolu and Rumeli Hisarı is the canonical Bosphorus moment.

# ASIA

## 🇰🇷 South Korea

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Bow when greeting — depth and duration scale with age and seniority of the other party
- Use both hands when receiving a business card, gift, or drink from someone older or senior
- Pour for the older or senior person at the table; never pour for yourself
- Remove shoes when entering any home, traditional restaurant, or temple
- Use family name first when introduced Korean-style (Park Geun-hye), and respect academic titles

**Avoid**
- Writing names in red ink — historically used only for the deceased
- Sticking chopsticks upright in rice — funeral symbolism
- Refusing the first drink at a meal with elders or seniors — accept and turn the head when drinking
- Using the country name "Korea" without specifying *South* — the distinction is felt
- Touching the head of any adult, or putting your feet near food

### Core Value
*Jeong* — the deep emotional bond that develops between people through shared time, food, and obligation. Korean social life is structured by relationships and the mutual care they require.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect to elders, especially in language, posture, or pouring order. Korean social hierarchy is encoded in grammar, in seating, and in the order of every action — violations are felt even when not corrected.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
The eldest at the table eats first. Use chopsticks for solid food, a spoon for soup and rice; never both at once. *Banchan* (side dishes) are shared; rice and soup are individual. Drinking is performed for others, not for yourself — the youngest pours, with two hands.

**💬 Language Notes**
Korean uses *Hangul*, the most logical alphabet ever designed (1443). The honorifics system is grammatically encoded — speech levels, address terms, and verb endings change with the relationship. *Annyeonghaseyo* (hello) and *kamsahamnida* (thank you) earn credit; the slight bow is automatic.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Always wrapped, presented with two hands, and not opened in front of the giver. Quality fruit, ginseng, or alcohol is canonical. Avoid sets of four (sounds like *death*).

**👔 Dress Code**
Conservative, well-tailored, and trend-conscious among younger Koreans. Seoul is one of the most fashion-forward Asian capitals; business is dressed; subdued colours dominate older or senior contexts.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 55%
- **Voice Expression**: 18%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 27%

### Origin & Chronicle
The Korean peninsula has been continuously settled for thousands of years and unified as a single state (Goryeo, then Joseon) for most of the past millennium. Five hundred years of Confucian Joseon rule, the Japanese colonisation (1910–1945), the Korean War (1950–1953), and the post-war economic transformation from one of the poorest countries on earth to a developed economy in two generations have shaped a culture of dense social obligation, fierce educational competition, and remarkable cultural export — the K-drama, K-pop, and Korean cinema generation are now globally consequential.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **CERAMIC · ✦ JOSEON HERITAGE** — *Kwang Ju Yo, Seoul*
   The contemporary ceramic house reviving the Joseon white-porcelain *baekja* and celadon traditions — Korean state-gift level.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A signed *baekja* moon jar is the canonical Korean state gift.

2. **HANBOK · ✦ HERITAGE COUTURE** — *Kim Mee-hee Hanbok, Seoul*
   The Bukchon couture house for *hanbok* — traditional Korean dress to commission, in the silk-and-ramie tradition.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Custom *hanbok* requires three weeks; rental is the alternative for a single occasion.

3. **TEA · ✦ KOREAN TEA HOUSE** — *Osulloc, Seoul*
   The Jeju-island tea estate — Korean green tea, *matcha*, and the country's serious tea-house tradition in modern form.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Insadong flagship has the heritage-grade ceremonial *matcha* not exported.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦✦** — *Mingles, Seoul*
   Mingoo Kang's three-Michelin-star room in Cheongdam — the most ambitious modern Korean kitchen, with the *jangs* (fermented sauces) at its centre.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full Korean-jang menu requires the wine pairing; the soju pairing is the local serious option.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦✦** — *La Yeon, Seoul*
   The Shilla Hotel's three-Michelin-star Korean room — the dignified version of *hanjeongsik* (Korean royal cuisine).
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full *hanjeongsik* tasting is the heritage protocol; allow two-and-a-half hours.

3. **BBQ · ✦ KOREAN INSTITUTION** — *Wangbijib / Born & Bred, Seoul*
   The serious Korean barbecue houses — aged *hanwoo* (Korean beef), the working canon of Seoul *gogi-jip*.
   *Tags: Business · Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The server grills; do not take over. The marbling-grade *hanwoo* is the meal's centre.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **PALACE · ✦ JOSEON ROYAL** — *Gyeongbokgung Palace, Seoul*
   The 1395 main palace of the Joseon dynasty — the changing-of-the-guard ceremony at 10:00 and 14:00 is the dignified protocol.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Wearing rented *hanbok* gives free admission; the *Hyangwonjeong* pavilion is the iconic frame.

2. **MUSEUM · ✦ NATIONAL** — *National Museum of Korea, Seoul*
   The 2005 national museum at Yongsan — the most architecturally serious museum in Korea, with the canonical Joseon and Silla collections.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Buddhist sculpture gallery is the spiritual heart; allow time for it.

3. **TEMPLE STAY · ✦ BUDDHIST** — *Beomeosa Temple Stay, Busan*
   The 678 mountain temple above Busan — overnight programmes for foreigners in the Korean Buddhist *templestay* tradition.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The 4:00 morning service is the spiritual core; the *baru gongyang* monastic meal is the cultural one.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *The Shilla Seoul*
   On Mt. Namsan since 1979 — the address of state visits, with the country's most established service tradition.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: La Yeon (in-house) is one of three three-Michelin Korean rooms; book at least a month ahead.

2. **PALACE HOTEL · ✦ ARCHITECTURAL** — *Four Seasons Hotel Seoul*
   On Gwanghwamun in central Seoul — the city's most architecturally serious modern hotel, with the Yu Yuan Cantonese institution and the city's top whisky bar.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Charles H bar is the city's serious whisky destination.

3. **HANOK · ✦ TRADITIONAL** — *Rakkojae Bukchon Hanok, Seoul*
   The traditional courtyard *hanok* in the historic Bukchon village — twelve rooms, the dignified version of the Korean traditional stay.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Heated *ondol* floors are the heritage; sleeping mats are the form.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ASIA-PACIFIC** — *Korean Air Business Aviation / Hi Air, Seoul*
   The Korean business aviation operators — Globals and 737 BBJs across Asia and trans-Pacific.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Gimpo handles business aviation; Incheon is the airline gateway.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ ESTABLISHED** — *KT Premium Limousine / hotel-direct, Seoul*
   The Hyundai Equus and Mercedes S-Class services for the embassy and corporate districts.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Tipping is not customary; service is included.

3. **RAIL · ✦ KTX** — *KTX Premium / SRT Special, Seoul–Busan & Seoul–Mokpo*
   The Korean high-speed rail business compartments — Seoul to Busan in two hours twenty.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The first-class quiet zone is observed; phones are silenced.

## 🇹🇭 Thailand

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with the *wai* — palms together at chest, slight bow, scaled to the seniority of the other party
- Speak softly always — Thai social life is performed at a much quieter volume than Western norms
- Show respect to images of the King and royal family — this is law as well as custom
- Remove shoes before entering any home, temple, or many shops; step over the threshold rather than on it
- Smile generously — the Thai smile is layered and the social lubricant of the country

**Avoid**
- Touching the head of any person, including children — the head is the most sacred body part
- Pointing the soles of your feet at anyone or anything sacred — feet are the lowest body part
- Disrespecting any image of the King — *lèse-majesté* law is severe and enforced
- Public displays of anger or impatience — losing face publicly is considered a serious failure
- Stepping on Thai currency — every banknote bears the King's image

### Core Value
*Sanuk* and *jai yen* — fun and a cool heart. Thai life is meant to be enjoyable and conducted with composure; visible struggle, anger, or seriousness reads as failure of character.

### Biggest Taboo
Any disrespect to the monarchy. *Lèse-majesté* (Section 112) carries serious criminal penalties, and even visiting foreigners are not exempt. The King is genuinely revered, and the cultural code is strict.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Thai meals are shared. Spoon (right hand) is the primary utensil; fork (left) pushes food onto the spoon. Chopsticks are for noodles only. Plates are filled in small portions and refilled. Rice is the centre; everything else accompanies.

**💬 Language Notes**
Thai is tonal (five tones) and uses its own script. *Sawatdee* (hello) and *khob khun* (thank you) — with male/female particles (*khrap*/*kha*) — earn real credit. The respectful particles are heard always. English is good in Bangkok, weaker elsewhere.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with the right hand or both hands. Quality fruit, chocolate, or wine. Open later, not in front of the giver, unless invited. The gift to the host's children is appreciated.

**👔 Dress Code**
Smart, conservative, and slightly more dressed than seems necessary. Bangkok business expects suits despite the heat. Temples require shoulders and knees covered for everyone.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 60%
- **Voice Expression**: 12%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 28%

### Origin & Chronicle
Thailand (*Siam* until 1939) is the only Southeast Asian country never colonised — a fact of considerable national pride. The Chakri dynasty has ruled since 1782, the Theravada Buddhist tradition shapes everything from the calendar to the everyday social grammar, and the post-war development from agrarian kingdom to manufacturing economy has been rapid. The country combines deep tradition (the temple, the royal family, the rice culture) with a modern, urban Bangkok that is one of the world's serious cosmopolitan capitals.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **SILK · ✦ THAI HERITAGE** — *Jim Thompson, Bangkok*
   The 1948 silk house founded by the American who revived the Thai silk industry — the canonical Thai gift, with the original house museum.
   *Tags: Business · Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Surawong flagship holds heritage prints not exported; the museum visit is part of the protocol.

2. **JEWELLERY · ✦ THAI GEMS** — *Lotus Arts de Vivre, Bangkok*
   The Bensley-Aschoff atelier — the Thai jewellery and home objects, with the gold-and-gemstone tradition reinterpreted.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The atelier visits are by appointment; the Mandarin Oriental boutique is the public counter.

3. **CERAMICS · ✦ BENJARONG** — *Royal Porcelain / Pinkaew Benjarong, Bangkok*
   The hand-painted *benjarong* (five-colour) porcelain — the Thai royal-court tradition revived in modern commission.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: A *benjarong* set is the canonical Thai state gift.

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦** — *Le Du, Bangkok*
   Ton Tassanakajohn's two-Michelin-star room — modern Thai cooking with farm-to-table Thai ingredients, named Asia's best restaurant 2023.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full menu is the format; *Nusara* (sister restaurant) is the heritage Thai room.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦** — *Sorn, Bangkok*

   > Etiquette tip: Walk-in queues form before opening; reservations are not accepted.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **PALACE · ✦ ROYAL HERITAGE** — *Grand Palace & Wat Phra Kaew, Bangkok*
   The 1782 Chakri dynastic complex — the Emerald Buddha, the most sacred image in Thailand, and the Chakri Maha Prasat throne hall.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Strict dress code (covered shoulders, long pants/skirts); arrive at opening to avoid the worst heat.

2. **TEMPLE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Wat Pho (Temple of the Reclining Buddha), Bangkok*
   The Reclining Buddha and the original Thai-massage school — older than Bangkok itself.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Foot-direction protocols apply at the Reclining Buddha; the school below offers the dignified massage.

3. **MARKET · ✦ FLOATING** — *Damnoen Saduak Floating Market / Khlong Lat Mayom, near Bangkok*
   The traditional floating markets in Bangkok's surrounding canals — Lat Mayom is the local-quality alternative to the tourist Damnoen.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Lat Mayom on weekends is the local serious version; private boat is the dignified way.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ ORIENT** — *Mandarin Oriental, Bangkok*
   On the Chao Phraya since 1876 — the Authors' Wing where Conrad and Maugham stayed, and Asia's most established grand hotel.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Authors' Lounge for high tea is the canonical Bangkok colonial-era ritual.

2. **RIVER HOTEL · ✦ ARCHITECTURAL** — *The Peninsula Bangkok*
   Across the river from the Mandarin Oriental — the city's most architecturally serious modern grand, with the river-fleet boats.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The river-suite category is the architectural booking; the hotel boat is the only dignified arrival.

3. **REMOTE RESORT · ✦ JUNGLE** — *Soneva Kiri, Koh Kood (Trat)*
   The Soneva resort on the eastern Thai island — the most architecturally serious remote resort in Thailand.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The cinema-in-a-treehouse and the Castaway dining are the signature programme.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ASIA-PACIFIC** — *Asia Aviation Pacific / Siam Land Flying, Bangkok*
   The Bangkok-based business operators — Globals and Falcons across Asia and the Indian Ocean.

   *Tags: Business*

   The classical Chao Phraya river dinner cruises — the dignified river protocol in the historic boats.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Sunset between Wat Arun and the Grand Palace is the iconic Bangkok moment.

## 🇻🇳 Vietnam

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a slight bow and a handshake; the bow is more important with elders
- Use both hands when giving or receiving anything important — gift, business card, drink
- Remove shoes before entering any home, temple, and many traditional restaurants
- Address people by their first name with the appropriate kinship term (*anh*, *chị*, *em*) — Vietnamese names are first-name primary
- Eat slowly and with visible appreciation — meals are extended, social, and shared

**Avoid**
- Touching the head of any person, especially children
- Pointing with one finger — use an open hand or a gesture of the chin
- Loud or impatient behaviour — Vietnamese social composure is highly valued
- Public displays of strong affection between unrelated men and women
- Discussing the war in casual terms — it is processed in Vietnam differently than in the West

### Core Value
*Tinh cảm* — the network of feeling, obligation, and care that runs through family and community. Vietnamese life is structured by deep familial and community bonds.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect to elders or to ancestors. The ancestral altar is in nearly every Vietnamese home, and the structure of address, seating, and serving order encodes the hierarchy of generations carefully.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Plates are shared, individual rice bowls are personal. Lift the rice bowl to your mouth; do not eat from the table. Chopsticks rest on the chopstick rest, never crossed and never stuck upright in rice. Serve the elders first, taste before adding sauce.

**💬 Language Notes**
Vietnamese is tonal (six tones in the north, five in the south) and uses Latin script with diacritics. *Xin chào* (hello) and *cảm ơn* (thank you) are universally appreciated. English improves rapidly among younger urban Vietnamese.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped (avoid black or white wrapping — funeral). Quality fruit (in even pairs), tea, or wine. Open later, not in front of the giver. Avoid handkerchiefs (associated with sadness) and clocks (associated with funerals).

**👔 Dress Code**
Conservative, modest, well-cut. Hanoi tends slightly more formal than Saigon. Temples require covered shoulders and knees. Business is dressed.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 53%
- **Voice Expression**: 17%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
Vietnam was a Chinese province for a thousand years before independence in 938, fought off the Mongols three times, expanded south against the Cham and Khmer, was a French colony for almost a century, fought wars of independence against France (until 1954) and the United States (until 1975), and unified under Hanoi after 1975. The country combines deep Confucian-Buddhist inheritance, a strong national consciousness forged in resistance, and the rapid post-1986 (*Đổi Mới*) economic opening that has produced one of Asia's fastest-growing economies.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **LACQUER · ✦ VIETNAMESE HERITAGE** — *Tan My Design / Hanoia, Hanoi*
   The Hanoi lacquer houses — traditional Vietnamese *sơn mài* lacquerware, in classic and modern designs.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A signed lacquer box is the canonical Vietnamese gift.

2. **TEXTILE · ✦ ÁO DÀI** — *Cao Minh / Hoài Anh / La Phạm, Saigon & Hanoi*
   The traditional *áo dài* couture houses — the Vietnamese national dress, made to commission.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A custom *áo dài* takes a week and is the traditional gift to a Vietnamese host.

3. **CERAMICS · ✦ BÁT TRÀNG** — *Bat Trang Pottery Village, near Hanoi*
   The 700-year-old pottery village outside Hanoi — the heritage Vietnamese ceramic tradition, with workshops open to visit.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Buying from the named master potters' shops gives much better quality than the tourist stalls.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦** — *Anan Saigon, Ho Chi Minh City*
   Peter Cuong Franklin's room in District 1 — Vietnam's first Michelin star, modern Vietnamese cooking.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The *pho ga* is the signature; the upstairs cocktail bar (Nhậu Nhậu) is the after-dinner.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HANOI INSTITUTION** — *Cha Ca La Vong, Hanoi*
   On Cha Ca Street since 1871 — the single-dish restaurant of *cha ca* (turmeric fish with dill), a Hanoi institution for five generations.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The dish is *cha ca* alone; do not look for a menu.

3. **PHỞ · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Phở Gia Truyền (49 Bát Đàn), Hanoi*
   The most respected *phở bò* (beef phở) in Hanoi — open mornings only, queues out the door.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Arrive before 9:00; the restaurant closes when the broth runs out.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HALONG BAY · ✦ HERITAGE CRUISE** — *Indochina Sails / Heritage Line, Halong Bay*
   The luxury overnight cruises through the limestone karst seascape — the dignified way to take the World Heritage bay.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Lan Ha Bay (further east) is the less-crowded alternative for serious cruises.

2. **MUSEUM · ✦ HISTORICAL** — *Vietnam Museum of Ethnology, Hanoi*
   The 1997 ethnology museum — the most architecturally serious museum in Vietnam, with the country's 54 ethnic groups.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The outdoor architectural park behind is the second draw; allow a full afternoon.

3. **HISTORIC · ✦ IMPERIAL** — *Imperial Citadel of Huế, Huế*
   The 1804 imperial capital of the Nguyễn dynasty — the dignified Vietnamese imperial site, restored after the war.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Forbidden Purple City is partially restored; the perfume river by *dragon boat* is the heritage approach.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ COLONIAL** — *Sofitel Legend Metropole, Hanoi*
   The 1901 French-colonial grand hotel in the Old Quarter — the address of Graham Greene, Charlie Chaplin, and the diplomatic Hanoi.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The original Metropole wing (not the Opera wing) is the heritage architecture.

2. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ BELLE ÉPOQUE** — *Hotel des Arts Saigon (MGallery) / Park Hyatt Saigon, Saigon*
   The architectural grand hotels of central Saigon — Park Hyatt is the address of state visits, with the most refined service.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Park Hyatt's Square One is the city's serious modern Vietnamese restaurant.

3. **RESORT · ✦ COASTAL** — *Six Senses Ninh Van Bay, Khánh Hòa*
   The Six Senses on a private bay near Nha Trang — the most architecturally serious coastal resort in Vietnam.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Hilltop Reserve villas have private pools and the bay's best views.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ INDOCHINA** — *Sun Air Vietnam / Hi Sky Aviation, Saigon*
   The Vietnamese business aviation operators — Challengers and Citations across Indochina and Asia.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Tan Son Nhat (Saigon) handles business aviation; Noi Bai (Hanoi) is more limited.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ ESTABLISHED** — *Mai Linh Premium / hotel-direct fleets, Saigon & Hanoi*
   The Mercedes service for the diplomatic and corporate districts — bilingual, well-established.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Hanoi morning traffic is severe; allow margin for early flights.

3. **TRAIN · ✦ REUNIFICATION EXPRESS** — *Reunification Express SE Class / private carriage charters, Hanoi–Saigon*
   The historic 1,726-km railway — private suite carriages on the Hanoi–Hue–Danang–Saigon route.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The full run is 33 hours; Hanoi–Hue (12 hours) is the most scenic single leg.

## 🇮🇩 Indonesia

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a slight bow and a soft handshake; many Indonesians follow with a hand-to-heart gesture
- Use the right hand only for giving, receiving, and eating — the left is considered unclean
- Remove shoes before entering any home, mosque, or many shops
- Speak softly always — Indonesian social life is performed at a lower volume
- Recognise the regional and religious diversity — Indonesia is the world's largest Muslim country, with significant Hindu, Christian, and indigenous populations

**Avoid**
- Touching the head of any person, including children
- Pointing the soles of your feet at anyone or anything sacred
- Public displays of affection — even hand-holding is uncommon outside Bali
- Using the left hand for any social interaction
- Treating Bali as representative of Indonesia — Bali is Hindu and atypical of the largely Muslim country

### Core Value
*Gotong royong* — mutual cooperation, the principle that the community works together as a unit. Indonesian social life is built on group consensus and shared obligation.

### Biggest Taboo
Religious disrespect, especially in mosques and temples. Indonesia is officially religious (one of six recognised faiths is required on identity cards), and casual irreverence — to Islam in Java, to Hinduism in Bali, to local traditions everywhere — is poorly received.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with right hand or with spoon and fork (knife is rare). Plates are often shared. *Nasi* (rice) is the centre of every meal, with side dishes around. The host invites the start with *silakan*. Coffee or tea is served at the meal's close.

**💬 Language Notes**
*Bahasa Indonesia* is the national language, designed to unify 700+ regional languages. *Selamat pagi* (good morning), *terima kasih* (thank you) are universal courtesy. English is good in Jakarta and Bali tourism areas; weaker elsewhere. Javanese, Balinese, Sundanese have separate honorific systems for elders.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with the right hand. Quality fruit, chocolate, or items from your country. Open later, not in front of the giver. Avoid alcohol unless you know the household is non-Muslim.

**👔 Dress Code**
Modest and conservative, especially in Muslim-majority areas. Batik is the formal Indonesian dress and appropriate at any major event. Shoulders and knees covered always in religious sites.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 60%
- **Voice Expression**: 12%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 28%

### Origin & Chronicle
The Indonesian archipelago has been a major trading crossroads for two thousand years — Hindu and Buddhist kingdoms (Srivijaya, Majapahit), Islamic sultanates from the thirteenth century, three centuries of Dutch colonial rule, the 1945 declaration of independence, the long Sukarno and Suharto presidencies, and the post-1998 democratic transition. The country is the world's fourth most populous, the largest Muslim country, the largest archipelagic nation, and a remarkable case of unity built on staggering diversity — *Bhinneka Tunggal Ika* (Unity in Diversity) is the national motto.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **BATIK · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Iwan Tirta / Batik Keris, Jakarta & Solo*
   The high-end batik houses — hand-drawn (*tulis*) batik in Yogyakarta and Solo court patterns, the Indonesian state gift.
   *Tags: Business · Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: *Batik tulis* (hand-drawn) is the heritage; *batik cap* (stamped) is the cheaper.

2. **JEWELLERY · ✦ JOHN HARDY** — *John Hardy, Bali & Jakarta*
   The Bali silver house since 1975 — the original Bali-based luxury jeweller, with the *kawung* and chain motifs.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Mambal compound visit (by appointment) is the Bali pilgrimage.

3. **TEXTILE · ✦ IKAT** — *Threads of Life, Ubud, Bali*
   The fair-trade textile cooperative — heritage *ikat* and other Indonesian weaving traditions, with documented village provenance.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The pieces here are heritage-grade; tourist *ikat* in Bali markets is mostly machine.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ JAKARTA INSTITUTION** — *Lara Djonggrang, Jakarta*
   The Anhar Setjadibrata-curated room in Menteng — Indonesian heritage cooking from across the archipelago, in a museum-like setting.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full *rijsttafel* (rice table) is the heritage Dutch-Indonesian protocol.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ BALI** — *Locavore / Mosaic, Ubud, Bali*
   The serious modern restaurants of Ubud — Locavore for the tasting room, Mosaic for the garden setting.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Locavore's full tasting requires booking weeks ahead.

3. **WARUNG · ✦ BALI INSTITUTION** — *Naughty Nuri's / Babi Guling Ibu Oka, Ubud*
   The classical Bali eating houses — Ibu Oka for the suckling pig, Naughty Nuri's for the ribs.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Ibu Oka closes when the pigs run out — usually mid-afternoon.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **TEMPLE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Borobudur Temple, Central Java*
   The 9th-century Buddhist temple — the largest Buddhist monument in the world, the spiritual centre of Java.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Sunrise from inside the temple grounds requires a separate Manohara Hotel package; otherwise the dawn from outside.

2. **TEMPLE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Prambanan Temple, Central Java*
   The 9th-century Hindu temple complex — the largest Hindu site in Indonesia, with the Ramayana ballet on full-moon evenings.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Ramayana ballet (May–October) is the dignified evening visit.

3. **CULTURAL · ✦ BALI** — *Pura Tirta Empul / Pura Besakih, Bali*
   The water temple of Tirta Empul (purification ritual) and the mother temple of Besakih on Mt. Agung — the spiritual centres of Hindu Bali.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: A *sarong* is required at every temple; bring one or rent at the gate.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ ARCHITECTURAL** — *The Hermitage, Jakarta / Mandarin Oriental Jakarta*
   The architectural Jakarta grand hotels — Mandarin Oriental for the central business district, Hermitage for the colonial-era heritage.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Mandarin Oriental's Lyon restaurant is the city's serious French.

2. **RESORT · ✦ BALI HERITAGE** — *Amandari / Amankila, Bali*
   The two original Bali Aman properties — Amandari for the Ubud rice-paddy setting, Amankila for the eastern coast.
   *Tags: Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Amandari is the architectural heritage; Amankila has the iconic three-tier pool.

3. **REMOTE · ✦ NIHIWATU** — *NIHI Sumba, Sumba Island*
   The remote-island resort on Sumba — once *Travel + Leisure*'s number-one hotel in the world, with the surf-school and the Spa Safari.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Sumba is reached from Bali by a charter flight; allow a full day either side.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ARCHIPELAGO** — *PremiAir / Whitesky Aviation, Jakarta*
   The Jakarta-based business operators — Challengers, Falcons, and the helicopter fleets to Bali, Sumba, and the Indonesian islands.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Halim Perdanakusuma handles business aviation; Soekarno-Hatta is for airline.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ JAKARTA** — *Blue Bird Premium / Silverbird, Jakarta*
   The Mercedes Silverbird service — the premium, well-established Jakarta chauffeur fleet.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Jakarta traffic is severe at all hours; the toll-road premium service is essential.

3. **PRIVATE BOAT · ✦ INDONESIAN ARCHIPELAGO** — *Aman Cruises / phinisi charters, Indonesia*
   The traditional *phinisi* schooner charters — the only serious way to take Komodo, Raja Ampat, and the Indonesian archipelagic ranges.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Aman *Amandira* is the architectural pilgrimage; private *phinisi* charters are the local-village option.

## 🇲🇾 Malaysia

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a soft handshake or *salam* (slight bow with hand to heart) — between Muslim Malaysians of the same gender
- Use the right hand only for giving, receiving, and eating
- Remove shoes when entering any home, mosque, and most temples
- Recognise the multi-religious, multi-ethnic structure — Malay, Chinese, Indian — each with its own etiquette codes
- Address professional and royal titles correctly — *Datuk*, *Tan Sri*, *Tun*, *Yang Berhormat*

**Avoid**
- Touching the head of any person, especially children
- Pointing the soles of your feet at anyone or anything sacred
- Using the left hand for any food or social interaction
- Public displays of affection, especially between unrelated men and women
- Confusing Malaysian Muslim, Chinese, and Indian customs — each operates by its own code

### Core Value
*Budi bahasa* — refined courtesy, the cultivated manner that holds the multi-ethnic society together. Malaysian social life prizes politeness, indirection, and the graceful avoidance of confrontation.

### Biggest Taboo
Religious or ethnic disrespect. Malaysia is officially Muslim but constitutionally multi-religious, and casual irreverence toward Islam, the Sultans, or ethnic relations is poorly received and sometimes legally consequential.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Malay meals use right hand or fork-and-spoon (knife is rare). Chinese meals use chopsticks. Indian meals use right hand. Halal protocols apply at Malay tables; pork is absent. Rice (*nasi*) is the centre of every meal.

**💬 Language Notes**
*Bahasa Malaysia* is official; English is widely spoken in business; Mandarin (and Hokkien, Cantonese) and Tamil are spoken by ethnic communities. *Selamat pagi* (good morning), *terima kasih* (thank you) are universal.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with the right hand or both hands. Avoid alcohol unless the recipient is non-Muslim. Quality fruit, chocolate, or items from your country. Open later, not in front.

**👔 Dress Code**
Smart, modest, conservative. Mosques require shoulders and knees covered, headscarves for women. Business is dressed despite the heat — long sleeves and trousers.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 55%
- **Voice Expression**: 18%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 27%

### Origin & Chronicle
The Malay peninsula has been a maritime crossroads for two thousand years — the Malacca sultanate, Portuguese, Dutch, and British colonial layers, the long Chinese and Indian migrations, and independence in 1957. Malaysia today is one of Asia's most successful multi-ethnic states, a federation of nine sultanates and four governor-led states, with a constitutional monarchy that rotates among the sultans every five years — and an economy that has moved from rubber and tin to electronics, palm oil, and Islamic finance.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **TEXTILE · ✦ SONGKET HERITAGE** — *Royal Selangor / Songket Sutera Asli, Kuala Lumpur*
   The heritage Malay textile and pewter houses — Royal Selangor pewter is the canonical Malaysian state gift, *songket* is the woven royal cloth.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A signed Royal Selangor piece is the standard Malaysian corporate gift.

2. **JADE · ✦ KL CHINATOWN** — *Galeri Petronas / KLCC luxury retail, Kuala Lumpur*
   The KL luxury retail axis at Suria KLCC — international houses and serious Malaysian brands in one mall.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The KLCC podium has the established luxury houses; Pavilion Bukit Bintang is the second axis.

3. **BATIK · ✦ MALAYSIAN HERITAGE** — *Jendela KL / Pucuk Rebung, Kuala Lumpur*
   The heritage Malaysian batik houses — distinctive from Indonesian batik, with the *cap* (stamped) and brushed traditions.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Malaysian batik is identifiable by its single-side print; Indonesian batik prints both sides.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦** — *Dewakan, Kuala Lumpur*
   Darren Teoh's tasting room — Malaysia's first Michelin star, modern Malaysian cooking with native rainforest ingredients.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full menu uses ingredients from the country's twelve states; allow three hours.

2. **HAWKER · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Restoran Lay Sheng / Madam Kwan's, Kuala Lumpur*
   The classical Malaysian heritage restaurants — the *char kway teow*, *nasi lemak*, and *laksa* of established houses.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Madam Kwan's is the dignified version; the original hawker centres are the local-quality.

3. **PERANAKAN · ✦ NYONYA** — *Indigo (KL Heritage Hotel) / Restoran Bibik Heritage, Kuala Lumpur & Penang*
   The heritage Peranakan-Chinese (Nyonya) restaurants — the Malacca-Penang colonial culinary tradition.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Penang Peranakan is materially deeper than KL's; the Penang trip is the heritage protocol.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **MOSQUE · ✦ ARCHITECTURAL** — *Putra Mosque, Putrajaya*
   The pink-domed mosque on the lake at Putrajaya — Malaysia's most architecturally serious modern mosque.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Robes are provided at the entrance; visit outside prayer hours.

2. **HERITAGE · ✦ GEORGE TOWN** — *George Town, Penang*
   The UNESCO heritage core of Penang — Peranakan mansions, colonial architecture, and the deepest Malaysian heritage food scene.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Cheong Fatt Tze (the Blue Mansion) is the architectural pilgrimage; book the tour and the dinner.

3. **NATURE · ✦ TAMAN NEGARA** — *Taman Negara, Pahang*
   The 130-million-year-old rainforest — the oldest tropical forest in the world, with the canopy walkway and orang-asli villages.
   *Tags: Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The dignified tour is from a luxury jungle camp; do not attempt without a guide.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ KL** — *Mandarin Oriental, Kuala Lumpur*
   At the foot of the Petronas Towers in KLCC — the city's most architecturally serious grand, with the iconic Towers view.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Towers-view rooms are requested specifically; the Club lounge has the city's best terrace.

2. **HERITAGE HOTEL · ✦ COLONIAL** — *The Majestic Malacca / Eastern & Oriental Penang*
   The two heritage colonial-era hotels — E&O for the British colonial Penang, Majestic for the heritage Malaysian Malacca.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: E&O's Heritage Wing rooms are the architectural booking; the Sarkies Bar is the heritage round.

3. **JUNGLE RESORT · ✦ BORNEO** — *The Datai Langkawi / Banjaran Hotsprings Retreat*
   The architectural rainforest resorts — Datai on Langkawi for the beach, Banjaran for the limestone-cave hot springs.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Datai is in the world's oldest rainforest; the resort's nature programme is the local protocol.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ASEAN** — *Aerocharter / Sayap Aviation, Kuala Lumpur*
   The KL-based business operators — Globals and Falcons across ASEAN.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Subang (the old KL airport) handles business aviation; KLIA is for airline.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ KL** — *Mayflower Limousine / hotel-direct fleets, Kuala Lumpur*
   The Mercedes service for the diplomatic and KLCC business districts.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: KL traffic is severe before 9:30 and after 17:00; allow margin.

3. **HELICOPTER · ✦ CHARTER** — *Sayap Aviation Helicopter, Kuala Lumpur*
   The KL-based helicopter charter — for transfers to the Cameron Highlands, Langkawi, and the east coast.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: KL to Langkawi is forty minutes by helicopter, four hours by road plus ferry.

## 🇵🇭 Philippines

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a warm handshake; younger Filipinos may *mano* (touch the back of an elder's hand to forehead)
- Use *po* and *opo* with elders to convey respect — these are non-translatable particles of address
- Smile generously — the Filipino smile is layered and the social baseline
- Recognise the deep familial structure — *bayanihan* and family-first thinking are foundational
- Acknowledge the country's distinctive identity — Asian, Spanish-Catholic, American-influenced, but its own

**Avoid**
- Pointing with one finger — pursed lips or chin gestures are the Filipino way
- Direct refusal of an invitation — soften, defer, or accept gracefully
- Public anger or impatience — losing composure is a serious failure of *delicadeza* (sense of propriety)
- Treating the country as merely Asian or merely Hispanic — it is its own combination
- Insisting on splitting the bill when invited — the host pays, and the form will be defended

### Core Value
*Hiya* and *delicadeza* — shame and propriety, the cultivated sense of how to behave that prevents social embarrassment for yourself and others. Filipino courtesy is structural and runs deep.

### Biggest Taboo
Causing public loss of face — direct contradiction, loud disagreement, or visible anger toward someone in front of others. The Filipino preference is for indirection, mediation, and the preservation of relationships above outcomes.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Filipino meals use spoon (right) and fork (left), or hands at heritage meals. *Kamayan* (eating with hands on banana leaves) is the celebratory format. The host invites with *kainan na* (let's eat). Plates are shared; rice is the centre.

**💬 Language Notes**
Filipino (Tagalog-based) is national; English is co-official and universal in business and education. *Magandang umaga* (good morning), *salamat* (thank you), and the elder-respect *po* earn real credit. Many regional languages exist (Cebuano, Ilocano, Hiligaynon).

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented warmly. *Pasalubong* — bringing back a gift from any trip — is structural in Filipino culture. Quality chocolate, food items from your country, or wine are well received.

**👔 Dress Code**
Smart, neat, slightly more dressed than seems necessary for the climate. The *barong tagalog* is the formal Filipino men's dress and appropriate at weddings, government events, and major occasions.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 38%
- **Voice Expression**: 32%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
The Philippines is a 7,641-island archipelago with three centuries of Spanish rule (1565–1898), forty-eight years of American colonial period (1898–1946), and Japanese occupation (1942–1945) — producing a culture unlike any other in Asia. Catholicism (the only majority-Catholic Asian country), Spanish surnames, American English, and pre-Hispanic Malay foundations layer into a national identity that combines Asian familism with Hispanic warmth and American institutional vocabulary. Manila has been a major trade entrepôt since the Galleon trade; the country is the world's largest source of nurses and seafarers.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **PEARLS · ✦ SOUTH SEA** — *Jewelmer, Manila*
   The Philippine South Sea pearl house — the country's distinctive *golden* pearls, cultivated in Palawan.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Philippine golden South Sea pearls are unique to the country; certified through the Pearl Council.

2. **TEXTILE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Kultura Filipino / Rustan's, Manila*
   The heritage Filipino textile and craft houses — *piña* (pineapple-fibre) cloth, *abaca* weave, and the working canon of Philippine craft.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: A *barong* in *piña* is the canonical Filipino men's gift.

3. **CIGARS · ✦ TABACALERA** — *La Flor de la Isabela, Manila*
   The 1881 Manila cigar house — the original Philippine cigar tradition, predating the country's American period.
   *Tags: Business · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Tabacalera Coronas Larga is the heritage Manila gift.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦** — *Toyo Eatery, Manila*
   Jordy Navarra's room — the Philippines' first Michelin star, modern Filipino cooking with deep regional sourcing.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The *Bahay Kubo* tasting (eighteen vegetables from the folk song) is the signature.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MANILA INSTITUTION** — *Antonio's, Tagaytay*
   The Antonio Escalante room in Tagaytay — the most established serious Filipino-French restaurant outside Manila.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Tagaytay setting (one hour from Manila, on the Taal volcano view) is half the experience.

3. **TURO-TURO · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Abe / Manam, Manila*
   The heritage Filipino regional restaurants — Abe (Pampangan), Manam (Pan-Filipino) — the working canon of Filipino cooking in dignified form.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The *kare-kare*, *crispy pata*, and *sinigang* are the canonical orders.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HERITAGE · ✦ INTRAMUROS** — *Intramuros & San Agustin Church, Manila*
   The walled Spanish-colonial city core — San Agustin is the oldest stone church in the Philippines and a UNESCO heritage site.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The *kalesa* (horse carriage) tour of Intramuros is the heritage format.

2. **NATURE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Banaue Rice Terraces / Chocolate Hills, Luzon & Bohol*
   The 2,000-year-old Banaue terraces and the geological Chocolate Hills — the Philippine landscape pilgrimages.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Banaue requires a flight to Cauayan and several hours of driving; allow two nights.

3. **DIVING · ✦ TUBBATAHA** — *Tubbataha Reef / Apo Reef, Sulu Sea*
   The UNESCO Tubbataha and Apo Reef diving — among the world's most pristine coral reefs.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Tubbataha is liveaboard-only and weather-windowed (March–June).

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *The Peninsula Manila*
   In Makati's central business district — the city's most established grand hotel, with the lobby that is the social Manila.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Lobby is the canonical Manila meeting point for business and high tea.

2. **HERITAGE HOTEL · ✦ COLONIAL** — *The Manila Hotel, Manila*
   The 1912 hotel facing the bay — the address of MacArthur, Hemingway, and three centuries of Manila's establishment.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The MacArthur Suite is the heritage booking; the bay-view rooms watch the famous sunset.

3. **ISLAND RESORT · ✦ AMAN** — *Amanpulo, Pamalican Island, Palawan*
   The Aman island resort on Pamalican — forty *casitas* on a private island in the Sulu Sea.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Aman charter from Manila is the only access; bookings are tight in March–May.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ARCHIPELAGO** — *Asian Aerospace / Royhle Aviation, Manila*
   The Manila-based business operators — Citations and Challengers across the 7,000-island archipelago.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: NAIA Terminal 4 (general aviation) handles business aviation.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ MAKATI** — *MGE Limousines / hotel-direct, Manila*
   The Mercedes service for Makati and BGC — bilingual and well-established.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Manila traffic is among the world's worst; allow material margin.

3. **PRIVATE BOAT · ✦ PALAWAN** — *Aman Cruises / Tao Philippines / private *banca* charters, Palawan*
   The traditional outrigger *banca* charters — the only serious way to take El Nido, Coron, and the Palawan island chains.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Coron-El Nido island-hop multi-day private charter is the heritage Palawan trip.

## 🇭🇰 Hong Kong

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a soft handshake and slight bow; among Chinese Hong Kongers, business cards exchanged with two hands
- Use both hands when receiving a business card; read it before putting away
- Address senior figures by title and surname (*Mr Chan*, *Dr Lee*) until invited otherwise
- Pour tea for the older or senior person at the table; never pour for yourself first
- Recognise that Hong Kong remains distinct in culture, law, and pace from mainland China

**Avoid**
- Sticking chopsticks upright in rice — funeral symbolism
- Tapping rice bowl with chopsticks — beggar gesture, deeply rude
- Discussing the 2019 protests, Beijing politics, or *one country, two systems* with people you do not know well
- Confusing Hong Kong Cantonese culture with mainland Mandarin culture — the distinction is felt
- Loud or aggressive behaviour, especially in restaurants — Hong Kong public life is fast but not loud

### Core Value
*Mou man tai* — "no problem" — the Hong Kong attitude of fast, efficient, can-do pragmatism. Hong Kong life is structured around speed, discretion, and getting things done.

### Biggest Taboo
Public political discussion. Since 2020, the political situation in Hong Kong has been tense, and conversations that were unremarkable five years ago can now have legal consequences. Visitors should avoid initiating these topics.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Cantonese meals use chopsticks (resting on the chopstick rest, never crossed). The lazy Susan is shared; serve the elders first. Tea is poured for others, never for yourself; tap two fingers on the table to thank the pourer (the *kowtow* substitute).

**💬 Language Notes**
Cantonese is the everyday language; English is co-official and universal in business; Mandarin (Putonghua) increasingly common. *Nei hou* (hello) and *m̀h-gōi* (thank you/please, when asking) earn credit. Cantonese is tonal (six tones) and unrelated to Mandarin's pronunciation.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped (avoid white or blue — funeral colours; red and gold are auspicious). Presented with two hands, not opened in front. Avoid clocks (sound like *funeral*), knives (cut the relationship), and sets of four.

**👔 Dress Code**
Sharp, well-tailored, brand-aware. Hong Kong is one of the most fashion-conscious cities in Asia. Business is dressed; designer labels appropriate; air-conditioning means full suits all year.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 50%
- **Voice Expression**: 22%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 28%

### Origin & Chronicle
Hong Kong was a British colony from 1842 to 1997, then a Special Administrative Region of China under the *one country, two systems* framework. The 150 years of British rule and the post-1949 mainland refugee influx produced one of the world's most distinctive city cultures — Cantonese language, common-law system, free-port economy, and a pace of life sustained by a population density rarely matched. The post-2020 political reorganisation has reshaped the city's institutions, but the working culture, the cuisine, and the visual character remain among Asia's most particular.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **JEWELLERY · ✦ HERITAGE JEWELLER** — *Chow Tai Fook / Chow Sang Sang, Hong Kong*
   The Hong Kong heritage jewellery houses — gold and jade in the Cantonese tradition, with the documented *chuk kam* (pure gold) standard.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: 24K *chuk kam* gold is the Cantonese wedding gift; the Mid-Autumn jewellery is heritage.

2. **TAILORING · ✦ HONG KONG TRADITION** — *Sam's Tailor / W. W. Chan & Sons, Hong Kong*
   The Hong Kong bespoke houses — Sam's for the rapid (24-hour) suit, Chan for the heritage Shanghai cut.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Chan's Shanghai-trained cut is the dignified bespoke; allow three fittings over two trips.

3. **TEA · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Lock Cha Tea Shop, Hong Kong*
   The Hollywood Road heritage tea house — Chinese tea in the working tradition, with the *gongfu* tea-ceremony service.
   *Tags: Friendly · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: A vintage *pu-erh* cake is the heritage Hong Kong gift.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦✦** — *Lung King Heen, Hong Kong*
   The Four Seasons' three-Michelin-star Cantonese room — the world's first three-star Cantonese restaurant.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Dim sum at lunch is the most accessible serious booking; the dinner tasting is the formal protocol.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦✦** — *T'ang Court / 8½ Otto e Mezzo BOMBANA, Hong Kong*
   The two other three-star options — T'ang Court (Cantonese) at the Langham, 8½ (Italian) at the Landmark.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: 8½ is the only three-star Italian outside Italy; the *cucina* is fully traditional.

3. **DIM SUM · ✦ HONG KONG INSTITUTION** — *Lin Heung Tea House / Maxim's Palace, Hong Kong*
   The heritage Hong Kong dim sum institutions — Lin Heung is the original 1928 trolley-cart dim sum, Maxim's Palace is the City Hall heritage.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Lin Heung is loud, fast, and traditional; arrive before 11:00 to get the trolley experience.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **VIEWPOINT · ✦ PEAK** — *Victoria Peak, Hong Kong*
   The Peak Tram and the harbour view — Hong Kong's defining landscape, best at sunset.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Peak Tram queue is severe; the private hire-car or the back-side approach is the local solution.

2. **TEMPLE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Man Mo Temple / Wong Tai Sin Temple, Hong Kong*
   The heritage Hong Kong temples — Man Mo for the Hollywood Road heritage, Wong Tai Sin for the working religious site.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The incense coils at Man Mo are the architectural protocol; bring a handkerchief for the smoke.

3. **HARBOUR · ✦ STAR FERRY** — *Star Ferry & Symphony of Lights, Hong Kong*
   The 1888 cross-harbour ferry and the 8:00 PM nightly light show — the canonical Hong Kong evening.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The upper deck is the heritage seating; both directions are eight Hong Kong dollars.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ HARBOUR ICON** — *The Peninsula Hong Kong*
   The 1928 Kowloon-side grand hotel — the address of state visits, with the Rolls-Royce fleet and the high-tea institution.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Peninsula's high tea (3:00 PM) is the canonical Hong Kong colonial-era ritual; queue forms.

2. **HARBOUR HOTEL · ✦ MANDARIN** — *Mandarin Oriental, Hong Kong*
   On Central's harbourfront since 1963 — the Pierre, the Krug Room, and the Hong Kong establishment dining.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Captain's Bar has been the Hong Kong establishment lobby for sixty years.

3. **HARBOUR HOTEL · ✦ ROSEWOOD** — *Rosewood Hong Kong*
   The 2019 grand on the Kowloon waterfront — Hong Kong's most architecturally serious modern grand hotel.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The harbour-suite category is the architectural; the Manor Club lounge has the city's serious view.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ASIA-PACIFIC** — *Metrojet / HK Bellawings, Hong Kong*
   The Hong Kong-based business operators — Globals and 737 BBJs across Asia and trans-Pacific.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Hong Kong Business Aviation Centre at HKIA is the dedicated business terminal.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ HERITAGE FLEET** — *Peninsula Rolls-Royce / hotel-direct, Hong Kong*
   The Rolls-Royce Phantom and Mercedes services — Peninsula has the green Rolls-Royce fleet, the city's heritage.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Peninsula Phantom is the canonical Hong Kong arrival; book at room reservation.

3. **HARBOUR · ✦ STAR FERRY PRIVATE** — *Aqua Luna / private junk charters, Hong Kong*
   The traditional Chinese junks for harbour cruises — Aqua Luna is the dignified scheduled service, private junks for groups.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The full-moon cruise from Tsim Sha Tsui is the heritage evening.
