## 🇹🇼 Taiwan

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a soft handshake and a slight bow; many Taiwanese add a hand-to-heart gesture
- Use both hands when receiving a business card; read it carefully before putting away
- Pour tea or alcohol for others, never for yourself first; tap two fingers on the table to thank
- Remove shoes when entering any home, and many traditional restaurants and temples
- Recognise Taiwanese identity as distinct — the culture is Chinese, but the political identity is its own

**Avoid**
- Sticking chopsticks upright in rice — funeral symbolism
- Discussing cross-Strait politics or Taiwan-China relations with people you do not know well
- Loud or aggressive behaviour, especially in restaurants and public transport
- Tapping rice bowl with chopsticks — beggar gesture, deeply rude
- Asking whether Taiwan is a country, or whether it is part of China — the question itself is loaded

### Core Value
*Renqing* — the social warmth, mutual obligation, and considered courtesy that runs through Taiwanese life. Taiwanese hospitality is famously generous, and visitors are folded into networks of *guanxi* with care.

### Biggest Taboo
Casual political talk about cross-Strait relations. Taiwanese opinions are diverse and the topic is politically and personally sensitive — visitors should listen rather than initiate.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Taiwanese meals are shared on a lazy Susan. Chopsticks rest on the chopstick rest. The host invites the start. Soup and rice are individual; everything else is shared. Tea is the universal accompaniment. Toasts (*gānbēi*) are common at business meals.

**💬 Language Notes**
Mandarin Chinese is official; Taiwanese Hokkien is spoken in homes and the south; Hakka in some communities. *Nǐ hǎo* (hello), *xièxie* (thank you) are universal. English is good in Taipei business, weaker elsewhere. Traditional Chinese characters are used (not the simplified script of the mainland).

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped (red and gold auspicious; avoid white). Presented with two hands. Not opened in front. Avoid clocks, knives, sets of four. Tea, fruit, and quality alcohol are canonical.

**👔 Dress Code**
Smart, well-tailored, conservative. Taipei business is dressed in dark suits despite the heat. Younger Taiwanese are fashion-aware; the country is one of Asia's serious bespoke and craft cultures.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 48%
- **Voice Expression**: 20%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 32%

### Origin & Chronicle
Taiwan was an Austronesian indigenous island settled by Chinese migrants from the seventeenth century, briefly Dutch, then under Qing administration, then Japanese (1895–1945), and from 1949 the seat of the Republic of China after the mainland's communist revolution. The post-war military rule transitioned to a fully democratic society in the 1990s, and Taiwan today is one of Asia's freest, most prosperous, and culturally productive societies — a leader in semiconductors, with a popular culture (K-drama-equivalent in Mandarin) of substantial reach.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **JADE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Eslite / Jianguo Holiday Jade Market, Taipei*
   The Taipei jade market and the heritage Eslite bookstore — Eslite is itself a Taiwanese cultural institution.
   *Tags: Family · Business · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Eslite Xinyi is the 24-hour bookstore that became a tourist attraction.

2. **TEA · ✦ TAIWANESE OOLONG** — *Wang De Chuan / Geow Yong Tea Hong, Taipei*
   The heritage Taiwanese tea houses — Taiwan's distinctive *high-mountain oolong*, in the *gongfu* tradition.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: A vintage *Da Yu Ling* or *Li Shan* high-mountain oolong is the canonical Taiwanese gift.

3. **CRAFT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Yingge Pottery Town / The One Living, Taipei & Yingge*
   The heritage Taiwanese pottery town and the Lai Sheng-Chuan craft brand — the country's serious modern Taiwanese craft.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Yingge is forty minutes from Taipei by train; the dignified day trip.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦✦** — *Le Palais, Taipei*
   The Palais de Chine Hotel's three-Michelin-star Cantonese room — Taiwan's only three-star, with the canonical *Peking duck* protocol.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full Peking duck service requires advance booking and three sittings.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN ✦✦** — *Mume / RAW, Taipei*
   The two-Michelin-star modern Taiwanese rooms — Mume for the European-trained Taiwanese cooking, RAW for the André Chiang heritage.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: RAW's seasonal Taiwanese tasting traces the country's culinary year.

3. **NIGHT MARKET · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Shilin Night Market / Raohe Night Market, Taipei*
   The heritage Taipei night markets — the working canon of Taiwanese street food, *gua bao*, *oyster omelette*, *stinky tofu*.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Raohe is materially smaller and higher-quality than Shilin; the dignified night-market visit.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **MUSEUM · ✦ NATIONAL** — *National Palace Museum, Taipei*
   The world's largest collection of imperial Chinese art — moved from Beijing in 1949, the canonical Chinese-civilisation collection.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Pre-book the Treasures gallery; the *Jadeite Cabbage* and the *Meat-Shaped Stone* are the iconic pieces.

2. **TEMPLE · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Longshan Temple, Taipei*
   The 1738 Buddhist-Taoist temple in Wanhua — the spiritual centre of old Taipei.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Avoid prayer hours for serious visiting; the central courtyard is the architectural core.

3. **NATURE · ✦ TAROKO** — *Taroko Gorge, Hualien*
   The marble-walled gorge on the east coast — Taiwan's most architecturally serious natural site.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Silks Place Taroko hotel inside the park is the dignified base.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Mandarin Oriental Taipei*
   In Songshan since 2014 — the city's most architecturally serious modern grand hotel.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Café Un Deux Trois is the city's serious classical breakfast room.

2. **PALACE HOTEL · ✦ ICON** — *The Grand Hotel, Taipei*
   The 1952 Chinese-palace-style hotel on a hill above the city — the heritage Taiwan diplomatic and state hotel.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Plum Blossom Hall is the heritage banqueting room; the dragon-staircase escape is the architectural curiosity.

3. **HOT SPRINGS · ✦ HERITAGE** — *The Gaia Hotel, Beitou*
   The Beitou hot-springs district above Taipei — the dignified Taiwanese *onsen* tradition, in the Japanese architectural style.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Private hot-spring suites are the dignified booking; Beitou is twenty-five minutes from Taipei centre.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ ASIA-PACIFIC** — *EVA Airways VIP Charter / Win Air, Taipei*
   The Taiwan-based business operators — Challengers and Globals across Asia and trans-Pacific.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Songshan Airport (city) handles short-range business aviation; Taoyuan handles longer.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ TAIPEI** — *Taipei Limousine / hotel-direct, Taipei*
   The Mercedes service for Xinyi (the financial district) and the diplomatic quarter.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Tipping is uncommon; service is included.

3. **RAIL · ✦ HSR BUSINESS** — *Taiwan High Speed Rail Business Class, Taipei–Kaohsiung*
   The HSR business compartments — Taipei to Kaohsiung in 90 minutes, the dignified domestic alternative.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The quiet zone is observed; the HSR-issued meal box is the heritage domestic-rail order.

## 🇸🇦 Saudi Arabia

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with the right hand; *As-salamu alaykum* (peace be upon you) is the universal opening
- Accept the offered Arabic coffee (*qahwa*) and dates — refusing the welcome ritual is a serious slight
- Use the right hand only for eating, giving, and receiving — the left is considered unclean
- Address senior figures with full title — *Sheikh*, *Prince*, *Dr*, *Eng*
- Recognise the religious centre — Saudi Arabia is custodian of the Two Holy Mosques and the heart of the Muslim world

**Avoid**
- Public displays of affection between unrelated men and women
- Photographing anyone, especially women, without explicit permission
- Discussing Islam, the royal family, or the prophet's life critically — these are not topics for visitors
- Bringing alcohol, pork, or non-Islamic religious materials into the country
- Confusing Saudi customs with Gulf-generic — Saudi protocol is its own and stricter than UAE or Qatar

### Core Value
*Karam* and *iman* — generosity and faith. Saudi hospitality is sacred and structural; faith is the organising principle of public and personal life.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect of Islam in any form, of the Prophet, of the royal family, or of the religious authorities. The country's identity is built on its custodianship of Mecca and Medina, and casual irreverence is poorly received and sometimes legally consequential.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with the right hand or with utensils. Coffee (*qahwa*) is served in tiny cups, refilled until you tip the cup or gesture *enough*. Major meals are *kabsa* (rice and lamb), shared from a central platter. Pork and alcohol are absent.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic is the official language; English is widely spoken in business and tourism. *Marhaba* (hello), *shukran* (thank you), and the formal *as-salamu alaykum* with response *wa alaykum as-salam* are universally heard.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with the right hand or both hands. Quality dates, *oud* perfume, or items from your country. Avoid alcohol absolutely. Gifts to the host's children are appreciated.

**👔 Dress Code**
Conservative and modest always. Foreign men in business wear suits. Foreign women dress modestly (long sleeves, long skirts or trousers, neckline covered); the *abaya* is no longer legally required for foreign women but recommended outside major hotel zones.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 50%
- **Voice Expression**: 25%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 25%

### Origin & Chronicle
The Saudi state was founded in 1932 by King Abdulaziz Ibn Saud, unifying the Arabian Peninsula under the Wahhabi-Hanbali Islamic tradition. The discovery of oil in 1938 transformed the country's economy and global position; the *Vision 2030* programme of the current Crown Prince has begun a major social and economic opening, including tourism, entertainment, and women's expanded participation in public life. Mecca and Medina remain the spiritual centre of the world's 1.8 billion Muslims, and the Hajj pilgrimage brings two million visitors each year.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **PERFUME · ✦ OUD HERITAGE** — *Arabian Oud / Abdul Samad Al Qurashi, Riyadh & Jeddah*
   The Saudi heritage *oud* perfumeries — the country's distinctive *oud* (agarwood) tradition, in the high-grade Cambodian and Indian woods.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: A high-grade *oud* (*muthallath*) is the canonical Saudi gift; the bespoke layering is the protocol.

2. **DATES · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Bateel, Riyadh & Jeddah*
   The premium Saudi date house — the country's distinctive *Khalas*, *Sukkari*, and *Ajwa* dates, in heritage gift presentation.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A box of *Ajwa* dates is the canonical religious-context Saudi gift.

3. **GOLD · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Lazurde / Damas, Riyadh*
   The heritage Saudi gold jewellery houses — the Gulf's distinctive 21K and 22K gold, with documented bridal and ceremonial pieces.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: 21K is the everyday gold; 22K is the wedding and ceremonial.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Najd Village (Qaryat Al-Najd), Riyadh*
   The heritage Najdi restaurant in a recreated traditional mud-brick village — the country's most architecturally serious heritage Saudi cooking.
   *Tags: Family · Business · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Eat in the traditional *majlis* seating on the floor; the *kabsa* is the canonical order.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN-LEVEL** — *La Petite Maison Riyadh / international Michelin chefs, Riyadh*
   The international serious dining axis at the new Mansard and Ritz-Carlton — the country's establishing modern fine-dining scene.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The international names are the dignified business booking; the heritage Saudi venues are for cultural visits.

3. **HERITAGE · ✦ JEDDAH** — *Al Naqsh Heritage Restaurant, Jeddah*
   The Al-Balad heritage district restaurant — Saudi cooking in the historic Hijazi architectural setting.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Al-Balad UNESCO core is itself the visit; the restaurant is the lunch within it.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HERITAGE · ✦ ALULA** — *AlUla & Hegra (Madain Saleh), Northwestern Saudi Arabia*
   The Nabatean rock-cut tombs of Hegra (the lesser-known sister of Petra) and the AlUla oasis — the country's most ambitious tourism project.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Habitas AlUla and Banyan Tree AlUla are the architectural bases; allow three nights.

2. **HISTORICAL · ✦ DIRIYAH** — *Diriyah & At-Turaif, Riyadh*
   The 1727 founding capital of the first Saudi state — the UNESCO mud-brick complex now restored as the country's heritage axis.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Bujairi Terrace beside Diriyah is the dignified evening dining axis.

3. **PILGRIMAGE · ✦ MUSLIM-ONLY** — *Hajj & Umrah, Mecca*
   The Hajj (annual) and Umrah (year-round) pilgrimages to Mecca and Medina — accessible only to Muslims, with strict protocols.
   *Tags: Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Non-Muslims cannot enter Mecca or Medina central districts; respect the boundary at all times.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **PALACE HOTEL · ✦ DIPLOMATIC** — *Ritz-Carlton Riyadh*
   The 2011 Ritz-Carlton in the diplomatic quarter — the country's most architecturally significant modern hotel and the address of state visits.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The royal suites have hosted state guests; the gardens are the architectural showpiece.

2. **DESERT RESORT · ✦ ALULA** — *Habitas AlUla / Banyan Tree AlUla*
   The architectural desert resorts at AlUla — the Crown Prince's tourism flagship, in the Nabatean canyonland.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: October–April is the climate window; summer is unworkable for outdoor.

3. **CITY HOTEL · ✦ JEDDAH** — *Park Hyatt Jeddah / Ritz-Carlton Jeddah*
   The Red Sea grand hotels of Jeddah — the dignified business stays for the western Saudi commercial centre.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Jeddah corniche dinner setting is the heritage Red Sea evening.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ GULF** — *Saudia Private Aviation / NasJet / Sky Prime, Riyadh & Jeddah*
   The Saudi business operators — Globals, Falcons, and 737 BBJs across the Gulf and beyond.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: King Khalid GA terminal in Riyadh is well-equipped; the new Royal Terminal handles state aviation.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ DIPLOMATIC** — *Careem Premium / hotel-direct fleets, Riyadh & Jeddah*
   The Mercedes S-Class services for the diplomatic quarter and the King Abdullah Financial District.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Women travelling alone may now drive; Careem and Uber have female-only options if preferred.

3. **HELICOPTER · ✦ ALULA** — *Helicopter Tours AlUla / private heli ops*
   The AlUla aerial circuits — Hegra and Madain Saleh from the air, the architectural overview.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The morning slot has the lowest desert haze; the canyon flythroughs require permission.

# MIDDLE EAST & NORTH AFRICA

---

## 🇶🇦 Qatar

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with the right hand; *As-salamu alaykum* is the universal opening
- Accept the offered Arabic coffee (*qahwa*) and dates as the welcome ritual
- Use the right hand only for eating and giving
- Address senior figures with full title — *Sheikh*, *Sheikha*, *Dr*, *Eng*
- Recognise the small but sophisticated character of the country — Qatar is small in population but globally significant

**Avoid**
- Public displays of affection between unrelated men and women
- Photographing women without explicit permission
- Discussing the royal family or regional politics critically
- Wearing revealing clothing in public — even foreign women should cover shoulders and knees
- Bringing pork or alcohol from outside; alcohol available only at licensed hotels

### Core Value
*Karam* — generosity and hospitality. Qatar's citizens are a small minority in their own country and the cultural code values the family, the tribe, and the carefully considered welcome of the stranger.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect of Islam, the Emir, or the royal family. As in Saudi Arabia, the religious and political fabric is taken seriously, and the country's small size makes social offence rapidly known.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with right hand or utensils. Coffee (*gahwa*) is served in tiny cups and refilled until you signal *enough* by tipping the cup. *Machbous* and *ghuzi* are the ceremonial dishes. Pork absent; alcohol only at licensed venues.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic is official; English is universal in business. *Marhaba*, *shukran*, *as-salamu alaykum* are appreciated. Many residents are South Asian or Filipino and speak their own languages too.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with right hand. Quality dates, *oud*, or items from your country. No alcohol. Children of the host are remembered.

**👔 Dress Code**
Conservative but slightly more relaxed than Saudi. Foreign men in suits for business. Foreign women cover shoulders and knees in public; the *abaya* is not required.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 50%
- **Voice Expression**: 25%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 25%

### Origin & Chronicle
Qatar was a small pearl-fishing and Bedouin sheikhdom under the Al Thani family from the mid-nineteenth century, a British protectorate from 1916, and independent since 1971. The discovery of vast natural-gas fields (the world's third-largest reserves) transformed the country in two generations into one of the world's wealthiest by per-capita measure. Qatar today is globally consequential beyond its size — Al Jazeera, the 2022 World Cup, the Doha Forum, and an active mediating diplomacy across the region.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **PEARLS · ✦ QATARI HERITAGE** — *Al Majed Pearls, Doha*
   The heritage Qatari pearl house — the country's distinctive natural pearls from the Gulf, the original economic foundation before oil.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Natural Gulf pearls are certified separately from cultured; the distinction is felt.

2. **PERFUME · ✦ OUD** — *Amouage / Arabian Oud, Doha*
   The premium Gulf perfume houses — the country's distinctive *oud* tradition, with bespoke blending available.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Mall of Qatar and Lagoona Mall hold the heritage flagships.

3. **HERITAGE · ✦ SOUQ WAQIF** — *Souq Waqif, Doha*
   The heritage Doha souk — restored to traditional architecture, the country's craft, falconry, and spice axis.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The falcon souk is at the back; falcons remain serious cultural objects in Qatar.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN-LEVEL** — *IDAM by Alain Ducasse / Hakkasan / Nobu, Doha*
   The international serious dining at the Museum of Islamic Art and the major hotels — IDAM has the I. M. Pei building's view.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: IDAM combines Ducasse with Arabic-Mediterranean cooking; the museum view is the architectural draw.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Al Mourjan Restaurant, Doha*
   On the corniche since 1979 — the heritage Lebanese-Arabic restaurant of Doha, with the city skyline view.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The terrace at sunset is the canonical Doha evening.

3. **TRADITIONAL · ✦ SOUQ WAQIF** — *Parisa / Damasca One Restaurant, Souq Waqif*
   The heritage restaurants in Souq Waqif — Parisa (Persian), Damasca (Syrian), the immersive Arab dining setting.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The Souq Waqif evening dining axis is itself the visit.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **MUSEUM · ✦ I.M. PEI** — *Museum of Islamic Art, Doha*
   I. M. Pei's 2008 museum on a man-made island — the world's most architecturally serious museum of Islamic art.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Late afternoon for the corniche light; the rooftop café for sunset.

2. **MUSEUM · ✦ JEAN NOUVEL** — *National Museum of Qatar, Doha*
   Jean Nouvel's 2019 desert-rose museum — the country's national museum and one of the architectural events of the decade.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The narrative galleries are best in sequence; allow three hours.

3. **DESERT · ✦ INLAND SEA** — *Khor Al Adaid (Inland Sea), Southern Qatar*
   The UNESCO inland sea where the desert meets the Gulf — accessible only by 4×4, the dignified Qatar desert protocol.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The full-day desert programme with falconry is the heritage version.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ ARCHITECTURAL** — *Mandarin Oriental Doha*
   In Msheireb Downtown — the city's most architecturally serious modern grand hotel.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Liang Cantonese restaurant is one of the city's serious dining destinations.

2. **CORNICHE HOTEL · ✦ FOUR SEASONS** — *Four Seasons Hotel Doha*
   On the West Bay corniche — the established address for state visits and corporate Doha.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The marina suites are the architectural booking; Nobu in-house is the city's sushi.

3. **DESERT RESORT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Al Wakra Hotel Qatar / Al Najada Doha*
   The Msheireb-area heritage hotels in restored historic buildings — the dignified non-corniche option.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Msheireb is the heritage core; the corniche hotels are the modern axis.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ QATAR EXECUTIVE** — *Qatar Executive (Qatar Airways)*
   Qatar Airways' subsidiary fleet — Globals and Gulfstreams from Doha, the most established Gulf operator.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Hamad International Airport VIP terminal handles business aviation; service is hospital-grade.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Karwa Limousine / hotel-direct fleets, Doha*
   The Mercedes services for the West Bay business district and the diplomatic quarter.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Doha traffic is mostly manageable except during prayer rush hours.

3. **DHOWS · ✦ TRADITIONAL** — *Dhow charter, Doha*
   The traditional Gulf wooden boats for sunset and overnight charters — the heritage Qatar maritime protocol.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The corniche-and-pearl-banks circuit is the heritage Qatar evening.

## 🇪🇬 Egypt

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with the right hand; *As-salamu alaykum* is the universal opening
- Use the right hand only for eating, giving, and receiving
- Accept the offered tea (*shai*) — refusal of hospitality is a serious slight
- Bargain in markets — the haggle is part of the social transaction, expected and enjoyed
- Recognise the depth of Egyptian identity — five thousand years of continuity is genuinely felt

**Avoid**
- Photographing people, especially women, without explicit permission
- Public displays of affection between unrelated men and women
- Discussing politics, the military, or the President critically
- Wearing revealing clothing — even outside the conservative areas, modesty is expected
- Pointing the soles of your feet at anyone, particularly when seated

### Core Value
*Karam* — generosity. Egyptian hospitality is famously open-handed, and the host's obligation to feed, welcome, and protect the guest runs deep beyond Western expectation.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect of Islam, the President, or the military. The country has been politically tense in the past decade and visitors should not initiate political conversations with strangers.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with the right hand or utensils. Bread (*aish*) is taken from the basket and used to scoop. Tea or Turkish coffee closes most meals. Pork is absent; alcohol available at licensed venues. Meals are long and social.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic is official; the Egyptian dialect is the most widely understood Arabic in the world (because of film). *Salam alaykum*, *shukran*, *afwan* (you're welcome) are appreciated. English is good in tourism and business.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with the right hand. Quality chocolate, items from your country. Avoid alcohol unless you know the recipient is non-Muslim. Children of the host are remembered.

**👔 Dress Code**
Modest and conservative. Foreign men in business wear suits. Foreign women cover shoulders and knees. Mosques require headscarves and full coverage.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 40%
- **Voice Expression**: 35%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 25%

### Origin & Chronicle
Egypt's character was forged on the Nile across five thousand years of continuous civilisation — Pharaonic, Hellenistic, Roman, Coptic, Islamic, Ottoman, British colonial, and modern Republican. The 1952 Free Officers' revolution under Nasser, the 1973 war, the Camp David peace, the 2011 revolution, and the post-2013 reconstitution are the modern political layers. Cairo (twenty-two million people) is the cultural capital of the Arab world; Egyptian film, music, and intellectual life are read across the Arab-speaking world.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **PERFUME · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Khan el-Khalili perfumeries, Cairo*
   The 1382 medieval bazaar's perfume axis — the heritage Egyptian essential-oil tradition.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Ask for the *attar* (pure essence) rather than alcohol-based perfume; the difference is significant.

2. **PAPYRUS · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Dr. Ragab's Papyrus Institute, Cairo*
   The state-licensed papyrus institute — authentic papyrus (not banana-leaf imitation, which is the tourist version).
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Authentic papyrus has a certificate; tourist banana-leaf "papyrus" is the cheaper imitation.

3. **COTTON · ✦ EGYPTIAN** — *Mobaco / Concrete, Cairo*
   The serious Egyptian cotton brands — the original long-staple cotton, in shirting and home textiles.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Egyptian-made Egyptian cotton is the heritage; many "Egyptian cotton" products abroad are blended.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Abou El Sid, Cairo*
   The heritage Egyptian restaurant in Zamalek and Heliopolis — the canonical heritage Egyptian cuisine in dignified form.
   *Tags: Family · Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: *Molokheya*, *koshari*, *mahshi* are the canonical orders.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ INTERNATIONAL** — *9 Pyramids Lounge / Sequoia, Cairo*
   The serious modern restaurants — 9 Pyramids has the actual Pyramids view, Sequoia has the Nile view.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: 9 Pyramids' sunset view of Giza is the canonical Cairo evening.

3. **HERITAGE · ✦ NUBIAN** — *Nubian Restaurant Aswan / Anakato Lodge, Aswan*
   The Nubian heritage restaurants in Upper Egypt — the distinctive Nubian-Egyptian culinary tradition.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Nubian villages of Aswan are themselves the visit; the food is the entry.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HISTORICAL · ✦ PYRAMIDS** — *Giza Plateau & Sphinx, Cairo*
   The canonical Egyptian site — the Great Pyramid, the Sphinx, and the new Grand Egyptian Museum (opening fully 2024–2025).
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Early-morning private access (Mena House Hotel is the heritage base) is the dignified visit.

2. **MUSEUM · ✦ NEW NATIONAL** — *Grand Egyptian Museum (GEM), Giza*
   The new $1 billion museum on the Pyramids road — opening with the full Tutankhamun collection in original ensemble.
   *Tags: Family · Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Tutankhamun gallery is the destination; allow a full half-day for the rest.

3. **CRUISE · ✦ NILE HERITAGE** — *Sanctuary Sun Boat IV / Oberoi Zahra, Aswan–Luxor*
   The heritage Nile cruises between Aswan and Luxor — the dignified four-day or seven-day Upper Egypt itinerary.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: October–April is the climate window; book the larger cabins for the river-side view.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ COLONIAL** — *Sofitel Legend Old Cataract, Aswan*
   The 1899 Cataract Hotel — Agatha Christie's room and the heritage Upper Egyptian grand on the Nile.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Christie suite (1909) is the heritage booking; the river-view terrace is universal.

2. **PYRAMIDS HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Marriott Mena House, Cairo*
   The 1869 hotel built for the opening of the Suez Canal — the only hotel adjacent to the Pyramids.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Pyramids-view rooms are requested specifically; the gardens are the architectural heritage.

3. **DESERT RESORT · ✦ RED SEA** — *Six Senses Zighy Bay (Oman) / El Gouna lifestyle, Red Sea*
   The Red Sea coast resorts — the dignified Egyptian Red Sea is El Gouna; for serious remote, the Sinai Bedouin lodges.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: El Gouna is the dignified beach; Sharm el-Sheikh is the package-tourism axis.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ EGYPTAIR** — *Egyptair Premium / private operators, Cairo*
   The Cairo-based business operators — Falcons and Challengers across North Africa, Middle East, and Europe.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Cairo Airport's VIP terminal handles business aviation; arrange visa-on-arrival ahead.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ ESTABLISHED** — *Hilton/Mena House fleets / Limousine Egypt, Cairo*
   The Mercedes services for the diplomatic and Zamalek districts.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Cairo traffic is famously severe; allow generous margin.

3. **NILE · ✦ FELUCCA** — *Felucca charter, Aswan & Luxor*
   The traditional Nile felucca sailing boats — the dignified river protocol in the centuries-old craft.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Sunset from the Aswan corniche is the canonical Nile moment.

## 🇲🇦 Morocco

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a soft handshake among same-gender people; the cheek-kiss is for friends
- Use the right hand only for eating, giving, and receiving
- Accept the *thé à la menthe* (mint tea) — refusing the welcome tea is a serious slight
- Bargain in souks with humour and patience — it is the social transaction, not a battle
- Recognise the layered Moroccan identity — Berber (Amazigh), Arab, Andalusian, French — each part is felt

**Avoid**
- Photographing people, especially women, without explicit permission
- Public displays of affection between unrelated men and women
- Wearing revealing clothing in non-tourist areas — modesty is the everyday code
- Discussing the Western Sahara question, the King, or sensitive religion topics with strangers
- Pointing with one finger or with the soles of your feet

### Core Value
*Diyafa* and *barakah* — generosity and grace. Moroccan hospitality is famously elaborate, and the home and the meal are the central institutions of the culture.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect of Islam or the King (Mohammed VI). The monarchy is taken seriously; political discussion of Western Sahara is sensitive; visitors should not initiate.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with right hand or with the dignified bread-and-tagine protocol. Tagines are shared from a central dish. Mint tea is poured from a height; refilling is automatic. The host serves; do not reach across.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic is official; *Darija* (Moroccan Arabic) is the everyday spoken; Tamazight (Berber) is co-official; French is widely spoken in business and the cities; Spanish in the north. *Salam alaykum*, *shukran*, *bisaha* (good appetite) earn credit.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped (avoid alcohol unless you know the household). Quality items from your country, fine pastry, or *thé*. Open later, with thanks. Bring a small gift for the host's children.

**👔 Dress Code**
Modest and well-cut. The *djellaba* is the traditional gown and dignified at any event. Mosques require shoulders and knees covered for everyone (and many are non-Muslim restricted).

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 42%
- **Voice Expression**: 30%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 28%

### Origin & Chronicle
Morocco is the only North African country that escaped Ottoman rule, maintaining its own dynastic continuity for thirteen centuries — the current Alaouite dynasty has ruled since 1631. Berber, Arab, Andalusian (after the 1492 expulsion from Spain), and French colonial layers (1912–1956) have produced a culture of rare depth — the *medinas* of Fez and Marrakech, the Sufi tradition of Sidi Ahmad al-Tijani, the Jewish heritage of the *mellah*, and the post-colonial cosmopolitan cities of Casablanca and Rabat. The current King Mohammed VI has pursued a notable opening to the West.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **CARPETS · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Bert Flint / La Maison du Kilim / souk dealers, Marrakech & Fez*
   The heritage Moroccan carpet houses — Berber, Atlas, and Rif weaves, with the documented village provenance.
   *Tags: Business · Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Berber carpets are graded by knot count and natural-dye certification; the haggle is the protocol.

2. **LEATHER · ✦ FEZ TANNERIES** — *Chouara Tannery / Fez leather houses*
   The medieval Fez tanneries (still in 1,000-year operation) and the heritage leather houses — *babouche*, bags, and hides.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A sprig of mint cuts the tannery smell; the dignified leather houses are above the dyeing pits.

3. **CERAMICS · ✦ FEZ BLUE** — *Art Naji / Aux Merveilles de Fez, Fez*
   The heritage Fez ceramic houses — the distinctive cobalt-blue *zellige* and the *bleu de Fès* tableware.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Hand-cut *zellige* is the heritage; machine-cut tile is the modern shortcut.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN-LEVEL** — *Le Jardin Secret / Le Tobsil / La Mamounia restaurants, Marrakech*
   The serious modern Moroccan dining axis — La Mamounia's three restaurants are the heritage establishment, Le Tobsil is the dignified riad-dining.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Le Tobsil's set Moroccan menu is the canonical heritage protocol; allow three hours.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Dar Yacout, Marrakech*
   The heritage palace-restaurant in the Marrakech medina — the dignified version of the immersive Moroccan dinner.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Dress for the experience; the gnawa music and bath ritual are part of the protocol.

3. **CAFÉ · ✦ COLONIAL** — *Café de France / Rick's Café, Marrakech & Casablanca*
   The heritage colonial-era cafés — Rick's in Casablanca is the (very) self-aware nod to the film.
   *Tags: Friendly · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Rick's is a tourist destination; the local serious cafés are in Quartier Habous.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HISTORICAL · ✦ MEDINA** — *Fes el-Bali (Fez Medina), Fez*
   The 9,000-alley medieval medina of Fez — the largest car-free urban area in the world, the spiritual centre of Moroccan Islam.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: A licensed guide is essential; the medina is genuinely impossible to navigate alone the first time.

2. **DESERT · ✦ SAHARA** — *Erg Chebbi & Erg Chigaga, Sahara*
   The two great dune fields — Erg Chebbi (near Merzouga) is the touristy version; Erg Chigaga (near Mhamid) is the remote-luxury.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Scarabeo Camp at Agafay (near Marrakech) is the dignified day option; Erg Chigaga requires three days.

3. **GARDENS · ✦ MAJORELLE** — *Jardin Majorelle & YSL Museum, Marrakech*
   The 1924 Majorelle garden owned by Yves Saint Laurent — the dignified Marrakech garden visit and the YSL museum next door.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Pre-book online to skip the queue; visit early morning for the cobalt blue.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **PALACE HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *La Mamounia, Marrakech*
   The 1923 grand hotel within the city walls — the address of Churchill, FDR, and the heritage Marrakech.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The garden suites are the architectural booking; the spa is the city's most refined.

2. **RIAD · ✦ COURTYARD** — *Royal Mansour Marrakech / Riad Fes / Riad El Fenn, Fez & Marrakech*
   The heritage *riad* (courtyard-house) hotels — Royal Mansour is the King-built ultimate, El Fenn is the literary-cool.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Royal Mansour's individual riads are the architectural pilgrimage; allow three nights.

3. **DESERT CAMP · ✦ LUXURY** — *Scarabeo Camp / Erg Chigaga Luxury Desert Camp*
   The architectural desert camps — Scarabeo at Agafay (one hour from Marrakech), Erg Chigaga for the deep Sahara.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The lower-Atlas camps are the practical alternative when the Sahara is logistically demanding.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ MAGHREB** — *Royal Air Maroc Cargo / private operators, Casablanca & Marrakech*
   The Casablanca-based business operators — Falcons and Challengers across North Africa, Europe, and West Africa.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Marrakech-Menara handles serious business aviation; Casablanca is the airline gateway.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ ESTABLISHED** — *Mamounia fleet / La Sultana fleet / private operators, Marrakech & Casablanca*
   The Mercedes services from the heritage hotels — the dignified hotel-direct option.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Tipping ten percent in cash is the form, in addition to fare.

3. **PRIVATE TRAIN · ✦ ORIENT EXPRESS** — *Oriental Desert Express / Marrakech Express, Tangier–Marrakech*
   The Moroccan railway business compartments — the dignified domestic alternative to flights.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Tangier–Marrakech run is six hours through changing landscapes; the first-class compartments are quiet.

## 🇮🇱 Israel

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a firm handshake — Israeli social style is direct, warm, and informal
- Use first names from first contact, including with senior figures
- Engage in robust debate — Israelis enjoy argument and disagreement is not personal offence
- Recognise the religious and ethnic complexity — Jewish, Arab, Druze, Bedouin, Christian — each operates by its own code
- Respect the *Shabbat* (Friday sundown to Saturday sundown) — many businesses close, especially in Jerusalem

**Avoid**
- Loud public criticism of Israeli politics, religion, or the security situation
- Confusing Israeli Jewish customs with Israeli Arab or Druze customs — distinct cultures within one country
- Visiting religious sites in inappropriate dress — head coverings, modest clothing required
- Mentioning the Holocaust, the conflict, or terror attacks casually — these are not small talk
- Treating Hebrew and Arabic as interchangeable — both official, but distinct in use and identity

### Core Value
*Chutzpah* — the audacious directness, the willingness to challenge, the refusal to defer. Israeli social life is characterised by frankness, debate, and a famously informal manner.

### Biggest Taboo
The conflict, the Holocaust, and Israeli politics are not casual topics. Israelis themselves discuss these intensely; visitors should listen rather than initiate, and avoid quick judgements.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Israeli meals are sociable and shared. *Shabbat* dinners (Friday night) are the central family meal. Kosher rules apply at religious tables (no mixing meat and dairy, no pork, no shellfish). Coffee or tea closes the meal.

**💬 Language Notes**
Hebrew is official; Arabic is co-official; English is universal in business. *Shalom* (peace, hello, goodbye), *toda* (thank you), *bevakasha* (please) are appreciated. The Hebrew alphabet is read right to left.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented warmly. Wine (kosher if you know the household), chocolate, or items from your country. Open at once with thanks. Children are remembered.

**👔 Dress Code**
Casual in business by international standards — Tel Aviv tech is famously informal, Jerusalem more conservative. Religious sites require modest dress: shoulders and knees covered, head coverings at the Western Wall and synagogues.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 32%
- **Voice Expression**: 38%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
Israel was founded in 1948 on the ancient Jewish homeland, with subsequent immigration from across the Jewish diaspora — Europe (Ashkenazi), the Middle East (Mizrahi), Ethiopia, the former Soviet Union — producing a country of unusual cultural density. The conflict with Arab neighbours and the Palestinian question have shaped the national psychology. Israel is also a global technology centre (the "Start-Up Nation"), with one of the highest densities of scientific research in the world. The cultural inheritance — Hebrew literature, the kibbutz movement, the rebirth of an ancient language — is taken seriously.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **JEWELLERY · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Yvel / H. Stern Israel, Tel Aviv*
   The Israeli pearl-and-gemstone houses — Yvel for the pearl tradition, the country's distinctive design vocabulary.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Israeli design is its own; international houses are also represented but the local jewellers are heritage.

2. **JUDAICA · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Hazorfim / Ben Zion David, Jerusalem & Tel Aviv*
   The heritage Judaica houses — silver kiddush cups, menorahs, mezuzahs in the Israeli silversmith tradition.
   *Tags: Family · Religious*
   > Etiquette tip: A Hazorfim mezuzah or kiddush cup is the canonical Israeli home gift.

3. **CERAMICS · ✦ ARMENIAN JERUSALEM** — *Armenian Pottery, Jerusalem Old City*
   The Armenian-Israeli pottery houses — the distinctive blue-and-white ceramic tradition revived by the post-1922 Armenian community of Jerusalem.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The four Armenian Quarter ceramic houses (Karakashian, Balian, etc.) are the heritage.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ MICHELIN-LEVEL** — *OCD / The Norman / Catit, Tel Aviv*
   The serious modern Israeli restaurants — OCD's tasting counter, The Norman's heritage hotel kitchen, Catit's seasonal Israeli cooking.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: OCD's no-menu chef's-counter format is the dignified Tel Aviv tasting.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Machneyuda, Jerusalem*
   Yossi Elad's room near the Mahane Yehuda market — the country's most established serious modern Jerusalem cooking.
   *Tags: Friendly · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The market-driven Friday lunch service is the heritage protocol.

3. **HUMMUS · ✦ INSTITUTION** — *Abu Hassan, Jaffa*
   The heritage Jaffa hummus institution — open mornings only, the canonical Israeli-Arab heritage breakfast.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Arrive before 11:00; the hummus runs out by mid-day.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HERITAGE · ✦ OLD CITY** — *Old City of Jerusalem & Western Wall, Jerusalem*
   The four-quarter Old City — Jewish, Christian, Armenian, Muslim — with the Western Wall, the Holy Sepulchre, and the Dome of the Rock.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Religious*
   > Etiquette tip: Modest dress required at all sites; head coverings at the Western Wall.

2. **MUSEUM · ✦ HOLOCAUST MEMORIAL** — *Yad Vashem, Jerusalem*
   The world's most architecturally serious Holocaust memorial museum and research centre — Moshe Safdie's 2005 building.
   *Tags: Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Allow at least four hours; the Children's Memorial is the emotional centre.

3. **HISTORICAL · ✦ MASADA** — *Masada & Dead Sea, Israel*
   The Herodian fortress on the Judean cliff and the Dead Sea below — the canonical Israeli day trip from Jerusalem.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Sunrise from the top of Masada is the heritage timing; the cable-car alternative is the practical.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *American Colony Hotel, Jerusalem*
   The 1881 hotel in East Jerusalem — the address of journalists, diplomats, and the heritage Jerusalem.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The garden bar has been the unofficial Jerusalem journalists' club for a century.

2. **CITY HOTEL · ✦ TEL AVIV** — *The Norman Tel Aviv*
   A 1920s Bauhaus-restored hotel in the heart of Tel Aviv — the city's most architecturally serious modern grand.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The rooftop pool is residents-only; The Norman restaurant is the in-house Michelin-level.

3. **DESERT RESORT · ✦ NEGEV** — *Beresheet Hotel, Mitzpe Ramon*
   On the rim of the Ramon Crater in the Negev desert — Israel's most architecturally serious desert resort.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The crater-edge cabin rooms are the architectural booking; the stargazing programme is the heritage activity.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ MEDITERRANEAN** — *Ayit Aviation / Israir Private, Tel Aviv*
   The Israeli business operators — Globals and Falcons across the Mediterranean and Europe.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Ben Gurion's GA terminal handles business aviation; Sde Dov was closed in 2019.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ ESTABLISHED** — *Galim Limousine / hotel-direct, Tel Aviv & Jerusalem*
   The Mercedes services for the diplomatic and business districts.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Friday afternoon traffic before *Shabbat* is severe; allow margin.

3. **HELICOPTER · ✦ CHARTER** — *Chim-Nir Aviation / private heli operators, Israel*
   The helicopter charters for transfers to the Negev, the Galilee, and the coast — the dignified alternative for short Israeli ranges.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Tel Aviv–Eilat is forty minutes by helicopter, four hours by road.

## 🇯🇴 Jordan

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with the right hand; *As-salamu alaykum* is the universal opening
- Accept the offered tea or Bedouin coffee — refusing the welcome is a serious slight
- Use the right hand only for eating, giving, and receiving
- Recognise the deep Bedouin code that runs through Jordanian society — *karam* (generosity) is structural
- Address the King with respect — King Abdullah II and the Hashemite dynasty are widely esteemed

**Avoid**
- Photographing women without explicit permission
- Public displays of affection between unrelated men and women
- Discussing the Israeli-Palestinian situation casually
- Wearing revealing clothing — modesty is the everyday code
- Pointing the soles of your feet at anyone

### Core Value
*Karam* and *sharaf* — generosity and honour, in the Bedouin tradition that underlies all Jordanian social life. The host's obligation to the guest is sacred.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect of the King, the Hashemite dynasty, or Islam. The monarchy is genuinely respected; political talk should not initiate from visitors.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with right hand or utensils. Bedouin meals (*mansaf* — lamb on rice with yoghurt) are eaten from a central platter, sometimes by hand. Coffee (*qahwa*) is served in tiny cups; tip the cup or shake your wrist to signal *enough*.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic is official; English is good in business and tourism. *Marhaba*, *shukran*, *as-salamu alaykum* are appreciated. The Jordanian dialect is close to Levantine Arabic.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Wrapped, presented with right hand. Quality dates, *za'atar*, items from your country. Avoid alcohol unless known.

**👔 Dress Code**
Modest and conservative. Foreign men in suits for business. Foreign women cover shoulders and knees. Religious sites require headscarves and full coverage.

### Communicative Presence
- **Presence & Posture**: 50%
- **Voice Expression**: 25%
- **Language & Phrasing**: 25%

### Origin & Chronicle
The Hashemite Kingdom of Jordan was created in 1921 from the Ottoman provinces of Transjordan, with King Abdullah I (great-grandfather of the current King Abdullah II) descendant of the Prophet Muhammad. The country has accommodated successive waves of Palestinian, Iraqi, and Syrian refugees while maintaining unusual stability. Petra (the rose-red Nabatean city), the Wadi Rum desert, the Dead Sea, and the early-Christian and Crusader sites have made Jordan a serious heritage destination. The Bedouin tradition runs deep across the country.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **JEWELLERY · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Wild Jordan / Jordan River Foundation, Amman*
   The fair-trade Jordanian craft houses — heritage Bedouin silver, embroidery, and rural-women's cooperatives.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Jordan River Foundation is the heritage cooperative; profits return to rural communities.

2. **MOSAICS · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Madaba Mosaic School / heritage workshops, Madaba*
   The Madaba mosaic tradition — the Byzantine-Christian heritage continued in the modern town, with the school's graduate workshops.
   *Tags: Family · Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Authentic Madaba mosaics are certified by the school; tourist mosaics are mass-produced.

3. **DEAD SEA · ✦ MUD AND SALT** — *Rivage / Jordan Dead Sea cosmetics*
   The heritage Dead Sea cosmetic houses — the country's distinctive mineral-based skincare tradition.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Buy direct from the Dead Sea factory outlets rather than airport shops for serious quality.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Sufra Restaurant / Wild Jordan Center / Hashem, Amman*
   The heritage Amman restaurants — Sufra and Wild Jordan for the dignified, Hashem for the institutional cheap-and-canonical.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Hashem's *foul* and *falafel* on Prince Mohammed Street is the canonical Amman heritage breakfast.

2. **RESTAURANT · ✦ FINE DINING** — *Fakhr el-Din, Amman*
   The heritage Lebanese-Levantine restaurant in a 1950s villa — the established business-dinner address of Amman.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The summer terrace is the heritage seating; the *meze* programme is the dignified order.

3. **BEDOUIN · ✦ DESERT** — *Wadi Rum Bedouin camps, Wadi Rum*
   The traditional Bedouin tents in Wadi Rum — *zarb* (underground oven) cooking, the heritage desert protocol.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The *zarb* dinner is the canonical desert meal; allow several hours for the full ritual.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **HISTORICAL · ✦ PETRA** — *Petra, Wadi Musa*
   The Nabatean rose-red city — UNESCO heritage, the canonical Jordanian site, accessed through the *Siq*.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Two-day pass is essential; the second day reaches the Monastery and the High Place. *Petra by Night* is the heritage evening.

2. **DESERT · ✦ WADI RUM** — *Wadi Rum, Southern Jordan*
   The protected desert wilderness — the location of *Lawrence of Arabia* and *The Martian*, with overnight Bedouin camps.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The luxury bubble-tents (Memories Aicha, Sun City) are the dignified version; the simple camps are the heritage.

3. **DEAD SEA · ✦ FLOAT** — *Dead Sea, Jordan*
   The lowest point on earth — the float, the mud, and the Dead Sea spa hotels along the eastern shore.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Mövenpick and Kempinski are the established hotels; the Israeli side has different access.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ AMMAN** — *Four Seasons Hotel Amman / The St. Regis Amman*
   The two architectural Amman grand hotels — Four Seasons in the diplomatic quarter, St. Regis in Abdoun.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Citadel-view rooms at Four Seasons are the architectural booking.

2. **DESERT CAMP · ✦ WADI RUM** — *Memories Aicha Luxury Camp / Sun City Camp, Wadi Rum*
   The architectural luxury bubble-tents in Wadi Rum — the dignified desert-night protocol.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The transparent dome bubble-tents are the architectural booking; the heated tents are the practical winter alternative.

3. **DEAD SEA · ✦ KEMPINSKI** — *Kempinski Hotel Ishtar Dead Sea*
   The architectural Dead Sea resort — the country's most ambitious wellness setting.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Anantara Spa for the heritage Dead Sea mud-and-salt programme.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ LEVANT** — *Royal Jordanian Private / private operators, Amman*
   The Amman-based business operators — Falcons and Challengers across the Levant, Gulf, and Europe.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Queen Alia's GA terminal handles business aviation.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ DIPLOMATIC** — *Petra Chauffeur Service / hotel-direct, Amman*
   The Mercedes services for the diplomatic quarter and the King's reception circuits.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Petra and Wadi Rum transfer (4-hour drive) is dignified by Mercedes E-Class.

3. **DESERT · ✦ JEEP CHARTER** — *Wadi Rum Bedouin jeep / private operators, Wadi Rum*
   The Bedouin-driven 4×4 charters — the heritage way to take the desert.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The dawn and dusk slots have the best light; midday is too hot most of the year.

## 🇱🇧 Lebanon

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with three alternating cheek kisses among friends — left, right, left — and warm handshakes with eye contact in business
- Accept hospitality with grace; refusing food or coffee in a Lebanese home is read as cold and even hostile
- Switch fluidly between Arabic, French and English — educated Beirutis genuinely use all three in a single sentence
- Show appreciation for the host's table; food in Lebanon is a love language
- Treat religious diversity with care — the country is Maronite, Sunni, Shia, Druze, Greek Orthodox and more, often in one extended family

**Avoid**
- Reducing the country to its civil-war past or to its current crises — Lebanese people are tired of being defined by tragedy
- Asking a stranger their religion or sect — a deeply personal and politically loaded question
- Discussing Hezbollah, Israel, or Syrian politics with anyone you don't know well
- Splitting the bill among guests — Lebanese hospitality means the host pays, full stop
- Praising another Arab country's food over Lebanese cuisine — an unforgivable culinary slight

### Core Value
Hospitality, sophistication and resilience — Lebanese identity is built on cosmopolitan pride, family loyalty, and the conviction that beauty and pleasure must continue regardless of circumstance.

### Biggest Taboo
Treating the religious-political balance casually. Lebanon's confessional system — where political power is divided across eighteen recognised sects — is the foundational compromise that holds the country together. Outsider commentary lands with weight.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Mezze is the soul of the table — many small dishes shared, eaten slowly, with bread as the universal utensil. Always wait for the host's *sahtain* (to your health) before starting. The meal is long; rushing signals you have somewhere better to be.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic with Lebanese dialect is the mother tongue, but French was the language of the elite for a century and English now dominates business. *Hi, kifak, ça va?* is a real Beiruti greeting. *Yalla* (let's go) and *habibi* (dear) punctuate every conversation.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Bring sweets, French wine or chocolates when invited; flowers also welcome. Avoid lilies (funeral association). For business, branded items from your own country are appreciated. Gifts are often opened later, privately.

**👔 Dress Code**
Beirut is one of the most fashion-conscious cities in the Middle East — designer labels, polished shoes, and grooming matter. Conservative for religious sites and the south; expressive in Beirut, Jounieh, and the mountain resorts.

### Communicative Presence
- Presence & Posture — 35%
- Voice Expression — 35%
- Language & Phrasing — 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
Lebanon's identity grows from Phoenician seafaring trade, Roman temples at Baalbek, the Maronite mountain refuge, four centuries of Ottoman rule, and the French Mandate of 1920–1943 that drew the modern borders. Beirut became the Paris of the Middle East — banking, publishing, and fashion capital of the Arab world — until the 1975–1990 civil war devastated the country. Reconstruction in the 1990s, the 2005 Cedar Revolution, the 2020 Beirut port explosion, and the financial collapse of 2019 onwards have tested the nation repeatedly. What endures is a culture that treats elegance, intellectual life, and the dinner table as forms of resistance.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **DESIGNER · ✦ LEBANESE COUTURE** — *Elie Saab Maison, Beirut Central District*
   The flagship of Beirut's most famous couturier — the bridal and red-carpet house dressed by Hollywood.
   *Tags: Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Appointments only for couture; the ready-to-wear is appointment-light.

2. **JEWELLER · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Maison Tabbah, Beirut*
   The 1862 Lebanese jewellery house — the dynastic name of Beirut craftsmanship.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The heritage atelier is the destination; the engagement-ring tradition is centuries deep.

3. **GOURMET · ✦ DELICATESSEN** — *Sukkar Pasha / Patchi, Beirut*
   The luxury chocolate and sweets houses — the dignified Lebanese hospitality offering.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Patchi for chocolates, Sukkar Pasha for traditional sweets; the gift-box presentation matters.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ BEIRUT INSTITUTION** — *Em Sherif, Achrafieh, Beirut*
   The set-menu Lebanese feast — the dignified showcase of Lebanese cuisine for visitors.
   *Tags: Business · Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The set menu is mandatory; come hungry — the parade of mezze is endless.

2. **HERITAGE · ✦ FARM-TO-TABLE** — *Tawlet, Mar Mikhael, Beirut*
   Kamal Mouzawak's village-cook collective — the genuine Lebanese terroir kitchen.
   *Tags: Friendly · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: A different village cook each day; the buffet honours regional Lebanese traditions.

3. **MEDITERRANEAN · ✦ ICONIC** — *Liza, Achrafieh, Beirut*
   The Liza Asseily heritage house — the elegant Beirut dining room.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Achrafieh mansion setting is the booking; lunch on the terrace is the move.

**🎭 Activities**

1. **ARCHAEOLOGY · ✦ ROMAN HERITAGE** — *Baalbek Roman Temples, Bekaa Valley*
   The greatest Roman temples in the eastern Mediterranean — Jupiter, Bacchus, Venus.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Baalbek International Festival in summer holds concerts among the columns.

2. **HERITAGE · ✦ COASTAL** — *Byblos / Jbeil*
   The continuously inhabited Phoenician port — the heritage harbour town.
   *Tags: Family · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: Pepe Abed's old harbour restaurant for the heritage Byblos lunch.

3. **WINE · ✦ BEKAA** — *Château Ksara / Château Musar / Domaine des Tourelles, Bekaa Valley*
   The historic Bekaa Valley estates — Lebanese wine since the Jesuits in 1857.
   *Tags: Romantic · Friendly · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Ksara's caves date to Roman times; Musar's heritage red is the international name.

**🏛 Stays**

1. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ INSTITUTION** — *Hôtel Albergo, Achrafieh, Beirut*
   The Relais & Châteaux townhouse hotel — the discreet Beirut elegance.
   *Tags: Romantic · Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The rooftop pool and bar with the city view is the landmark.

2. **GRAND HOTEL · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Phoenicia Hotel, Beirut*
   The 1961 Beirut institution — the historic seafront grande dame.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The InterContinental management; the lobby is the diplomatic crossroads.

3. **MOUNTAIN · ✦ HERITAGE** — *Grand Hills, Broummana / Faqra Club, Mount Lebanon*
   The mountain-retreat tradition — the Beirut elite summer escape.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The summer-mountain migration is centuries old; July and August are the season.

**✈ Transport**

1. **PRIVATE AVIATION · ✦ MEDITERRANEAN** — *Cedar Jet Center, Beirut*
   The Beirut FBO — the private aviation gateway to the Levant and Cyprus.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: The Cyprus and Athens hops are 30–45 minutes; the Gulf in 3 hours.

2. **CHAUFFEUR · ✦ DIPLOMATIC** — *Hotel-direct chauffeurs / private operators, Beirut*
   The hotel-direct Mercedes services — the dignified urban arrangement.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Beirut traffic is severe; allow extra time for any cross-city movement.

3. **PRIVATE BOAT · ✦ MEDITERRANEAN** — *ATCL Beirut / private charters*
   The Mediterranean yachting tradition — the heritage Beirut Yacht Club connection.
   *Tags: Romantic · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The Jounieh Bay and the Cyprus crossings are the heritage routes.

## 🇴🇲 Oman

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet older men with "*As-salaam alaykum*" and accept the long, gracious response — Omanis are unhurried in greeting
- Accept *kahwa* (cardamom coffee) and dates whenever offered — refusing the first cup is rude; refuse the third with a hand-shake of the cup
- Dress modestly across the country, including tourists in Muscat — Oman holds traditional standards more firmly than the UAE
- Address the Sultan and royal family with respect — this is one of the most loved monarchies in the region
- Remove shoes before entering homes and many traditional buildings

**Avoid**
- Comparing Oman to the UAE — Omanis are quietly proud of their distinct heritage and slower, more dignified development
- Public displays of affection — Oman is more conservative than most Gulf neighbours
- Photographing Omanis (especially women) without explicit permission
- Rushing greetings or hospitality — patience is read as respect
- Bringing or discussing alcohol outside licensed hotel venues

### Core Value
Quiet dignity, deep tradition, and natural hospitality — Oman defines itself by graciousness, not by spectacle, and by Ibadi Islamic moderation rather than the louder modernity of its Gulf neighbours.

### Biggest Taboo
Treating Oman as a smaller Dubai. Omani identity is built on Ibadi Islam, the seafaring sultanate's centuries-old maritime trade, the Sultan Qaboos legacy of careful modernisation, and a refusal to chase the rest of the Gulf's spectacle. Omanis read this distinction as essential.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with the right hand only when dining traditionally; cutlery is also fine in modern settings. *Shuwa* (slow-cooked spiced meat) and *majboos* (spiced rice) are eaten communally from large platters. Coffee and dates start every meeting.

**💬 Language Notes**
Arabic with Omani dialect is the mother tongue; English is widely spoken in Muscat and tourism. Swahili is heard in coastal communities (Zanzibar legacy). The Sultan was always referred to as His Majesty Sultan Qaboos and now Sultan Haitham — full title, always.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
Frankincense from Salalah, Omani halwa, or quality dates are appropriate. For business, fine pens, leather goods, or items from your home country. Avoid alcohol or anything bearing imagery of pigs, dogs or partial nudity.

**👔 Dress Code**
Omani men wear the white *dishdasha* and embroidered *kummah* cap; women the abaya. Visitors should dress modestly: covered shoulders, long trousers or modest skirts, no transparent fabrics. Resort beach areas more relaxed but never topless.

### Communicative Presence
- Presence & Posture — 50%
- Voice Expression — 25%
- Language & Phrasing — 25%

### Origin & Chronicle
Oman's history runs through the maritime sultanate that once ruled Zanzibar and parts of the East African coast, the unique Ibadi school of Islam (older than the Sunni-Shia split), and the long Said dynasty. The 1970 transition — when Sultan Qaboos bin Said replaced his father in a quiet palace coup — opened Oman to the modern world after decades of deliberate isolation. Sultan Qaboos's fifty-year reign built schools, hospitals, roads and a national identity, while preserving Omani modesty and heritage. His successor Sultan Haitham (2020) continues the careful balance. What outsiders mistake for slowness is, in Omani terms, dignity.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

   The royal Omani perfume house and the heritage frankincense souks — the country's signature export.

# SUB-SAHARAN AFRICA

---

## 🇰🇪 Kenya

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with a firm handshake and *"Jambo"* or *"Habari"*; among Swahili speakers, *"Habari yako?"* with eye contact
- Use *Mzee* (elder) when addressing senior men — a genuine mark of respect
- Accept tea (*chai*) when offered in homes and offices — Kenyan hospitality runs through the cup
- Tip generously in safari camps and lodges — the staff are the heart of the experience
- Show interest in tribal heritage (Kikuyu, Luo, Maasai, Kalenjin, others) — Kenyans are proud of their distinct origins

**Avoid**
- Treating the Maasai or other communities as photo subjects without consent and a fair fee
- Discussing tribal politics with people you don't know — Kenyan electoral history makes this sensitive
- Public displays of affection — modest by international standards
- Photographing government buildings, military, or police
- Confusing Kenya with neighbouring countries — Kenyans take East African distinctions seriously

### Core Value
Pride in heritage and natural wealth, hospitable warmth, and a hard-working entrepreneurial spirit — Kenya sees itself as East Africa's leading nation, with a distinctly cosmopolitan capital and unmatched landscapes.

### Biggest Taboo
Treating Kenya as a generic "Africa" rather than as a specific, complex, modern nation. Kenyans are sensitive to outsider stereotypes that flatten the country into safari-cliché or poverty narratives. Engagement with the actual modern Kenya — Nairobi tech, Kenyan literature, the Kalenjin running tradition — is welcomed.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
*Nyama choma* (grilled meat) is the social meal, eaten with *ugali* (maize meal) shaped by hand into scoops. Wash hands before and after the meal — water is brought to the table. Wait for elders to begin. Refusing food in homes can offend.

**💬 Language Notes**
Swahili and English are both official; educated Kenyans switch fluidly. *Asante* (thank you), *karibu* (welcome), and *pole pole* (slowly, slowly) are the essential phrases. *"Hakuna matata"* is real Swahili but more often a tourist phrase.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
For business: branded items, fine pens, books from your country. For homes: tea, sweets, or items for children. Avoid alcohol unless you know the host. Gifts opened later, privately.

**👔 Dress Code**
Smart-casual in Nairobi business; formal for government and senior meetings. Safari clothing in neutrals on the reserves (avoid blue and black, which attract tsetse flies). Modest dress at the coast (Mombasa, Lamu) where Muslim communities are dominant.

### Communicative Presence
- Presence & Posture — 40%
- Voice Expression — 30%
- Language & Phrasing — 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
Kenya's modern identity grows from the Bantu, Nilotic and Cushitic migrations, the centuries of Swahili coastal trade with Arabia and India, the Imperial British East Africa Company, and the 1895–1963 colonial period that built the railway, the highlands settler economy, and Nairobi itself. Independence under Jomo Kenyatta in 1963, the Daniel arap Moi years, the post-2002 democratic opening, and the modern technology economy (M-Pesa pioneered mobile money here) have built the country's cosmopolitan capital. Kenya is also the global home of long-distance running — the Kalenjin highlands have produced more world-class marathoners than any region on earth — and the most photographed safari landscape in the world: the Maasai Mara.

   > Etiquette tip: The market rotates locations daily; the Village Market site on Friday is the established spot.

   *Tags: Romantic · Business · Family*

## 🇳🇬 Nigeria

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with enthusiasm and warmth — Nigerians are direct, expressive, and genuinely welcoming
- Use titles liberally — *Chief*, *Doctor*, *Engineer*, *Alhaji* (for Muslims who have made the pilgrimage), *Mama*, *Pa* — they matter
- Show respect to elders by bowing slightly when greeting Yoruba elders, kneeling for very senior elders if appropriate
- Be patient with what Nigerians call "African time" — schedules slip, but business gets done
- Eat heartily when offered Nigerian food — *jollof rice*, *egusi*, *suya* — declining hospitality is read as rejection

**Avoid**
- Calling Nigeria a single homogeneous culture — Yoruba, Igbo, Hausa-Fulani and 250+ other groups are distinct
- Discussing the Biafran war, North-South tensions, or religious conflict casually
- Confusing the legitimate Nigerian business community with the fraud stereotypes — Nigerians are sensitive to this
- Showing the soles of your feet when seated, especially toward elders
- Public criticism of the host country — Nigerians criticise their own freely but resent it from outsiders

### Core Value
Ambition, expressive confidence, religious devotion, and family loyalty — Nigeria is Africa's most populous nation, the cultural and economic powerhouse of West Africa, and a country that values success, respect, and visible achievement.

### Biggest Taboo
Disrespect of elders. Nigerian culture across all major groups holds elders in absolute reverence — kneeling or bowing greetings, the expectation that elders are always served first, the requirement that they speak first in meetings. Casual familiarity with senior people is read as profound disrespect.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
Eat with the right hand only when eating Nigerian food traditionally; cutlery in formal settings. Wait for the most senior person to begin. *Pounded yam with egusi*, *jollof rice* (the West African rivalry with Ghana is real), and *suya* (spiced grilled meat) are the iconic dishes. Never refuse food; small portions are acceptable.

**💬 Language Notes**
English (with Nigerian inflection) is the official lingua franca; Pidgin is the daily street language; Yoruba, Igbo and Hausa are the three major regional languages. *"How are you?"* — *"I dey fine"*. Honorifics matter enormously; "Sir" and "Ma" are everyday markers of respect.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
For homes: quality drinks (good wine, Hennessy in some circles, schnapps in traditional Igbo settings), cakes, or fruit baskets. For business: fine pens, branded items, or quality whisky/cognac. For traditional ceremonies, kola nut is genuinely heritage. Avoid lilies (funeral).

**👔 Dress Code**
Lagos business is formal — sharp suits, traditional Yoruba *agbada* and *fila* cap or Igbo *isi-agu* for senior men. Women wear traditional *iro and buba* with *gele* head-tie at major events; sharp Western dress in business. Northern Nigeria more conservative; modest dress for any visit.

### Communicative Presence
- Presence & Posture — 30%
- Voice Expression — 40%
- Language & Phrasing — 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
Nigeria's identity emerges from the great pre-colonial kingdoms — the Yoruba Oyo Empire and Ife (the spiritual home), the Igbo trading networks of the southeast, the Hausa-Fulani Sokoto Caliphate of the north, and the Benin Kingdom's bronze-casting heritage. The British Royal Niger Company and the 1914 amalgamation by Lord Lugard joined northern and southern protectorates. Independence in 1960, the Biafran civil war of 1967–70, the long oil-boom-and-bust cycles, and the modern democratic period from 1999 have shaped a country of immense cultural production: Nollywood is the world's second-largest film industry, Afrobeats is global pop music, and Nigerian literature (Achebe, Soyinka, Adichie) leads the continent. Nigeria thinks of itself as the giant of Africa — and demands to be treated as one.

### The Local

   The Reni Folawiyo concept store — the curator of African designers and the dignified Lagos luxury retail.

   > Etiquette tip: The David Adjaye-designed Victoria Island building is the architectural booking.

   *Tags: Business · Romantic*
   > Etiquette tip: The Ikoyi residential setting is the booking; the contemporary art collection is the architectural feature.

**✈ Transport**

   The Lagos FBO — the West African private aviation hub.
   *Tags: Business*

   The Mercedes and bullet-proof options — the dignified Lagos corporate arrangement.
   *Tags: Business*
   > Etiquette tip: Lagos traffic is among the world's worst; allow 2–3 hours for any Victoria Island to mainland transfer.

   The Lagos Lagoon ferries — the dignified water-bypass of the Lagos traffic.
   *Tags: Business · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: The Victoria Island to Ikoyi water-taxi is faster than the road; the heritage operators are well-established.

## 🇪🇹 Ethiopia

### Quick Briefing
*The five customs to know before arrival*

**Do**
- Greet with multiple cheek-touches (right, left, right) among friends and family — Ethiopians are warm and physical in greeting
- Show respect for the Orthodox Church — over 40% of the population is Ethiopian Orthodox, and faith permeates daily life
- Eat *injera* with the right hand only, tearing it to scoop the *wat* stews
- Accept the *bunna* (coffee) ceremony patiently — three rounds (*abol*, *tona*, *baraka*) take an hour, and refusing is a slight
- Show pride in Ethiopia's distinct identity — the only African nation never colonised, with its own script, calendar, and time system

**Avoid**
- Treating Ethiopia as a generic African country — Ethiopians take their unique civilisational heritage extremely seriously
- Discussing the Eritrean conflict, the Tigray war, or ethnic-federal politics with people you don't know
- Public displays of affection — Ethiopia is conservative
- Using your left hand for eating, gift-giving, or greeting
- Comparing Ethiopian Orthodox Christianity to other Christian traditions reductively

### Core Value
Pride in three thousand years of civilisation, religious devotion, and proud independence — Ethiopia views itself as the cradle of humanity, the Lion of Judah's seat, and the only African nation that defeated colonisation (the 1896 Battle of Adwa).

### Biggest Taboo
Suggesting Ethiopia was ever colonised, or implying Ethiopian culture is derivative of others. Ethiopia's distinct alphabet (Ge'ez), thirteen-month calendar (still seven years behind the Gregorian), unique Orthodox Christianity, and unbroken sovereignty are matters of profound national pride.

### Essential Protocols

**🍽 Table Manners**
*Injera* (sourdough flatbread) is the plate, the utensil, and the meal — torn with the right hand to scoop the *wat* stews. The *gursha* (feeding a guest by hand from your portion) is a deep gesture of friendship — accept gracefully. Wash hands before and after.

**💬 Language Notes**
Amharic is the working national language; Oromo is the largest first language; Tigrinya, Somali, and dozens of others are spoken regionally. *Selam* (peace, hello), *amaseganalehu* (thank you), and *ishi* (OK) are the survival phrases. The Ge'ez script has its own letters and direction.

**🎁 Gift Protocol**
For homes: quality coffee (Ethiopia is the birthplace of coffee), sweets, or fine spirits. For business: branded items, fine pens, books from your country. Gifts are received with both hands; opening immediately is acceptable.

**👔 Dress Code**
Addis Ababa business is formal — Western suits or traditional *netela* (white cotton shawl) for cultural occasions. Conservative dress for church visits; women cover heads. Highland coolness means layered clothing; traditional white *habesha kemis* for women is the heritage formal dress.

### Communicative Presence
- Presence & Posture — 45%
- Voice Expression — 25%
- Language & Phrasing — 30%

### Origin & Chronicle
Ethiopia's identity stretches from the Aksumite Empire (one of antiquity's four great powers, mentioned in the Bible), through the Solomonic dynasty's claim of descent from Solomon and the Queen of Sheba, the Christianisation under King Ezana in the 4th century, the rock-hewn churches of Lalibela built in the 12th and 13th centuries, the medieval kingdom of Gondar, the Battle of Adwa in 1896 (when Emperor Menelik II defeated Italy), and the long reign of Emperor Haile Selassie (1930–1974). The Derg communist regime (1974–1991), the federal democratic republic since 1995, and the Tigray war of 2020–2022 have shaped the modern state. Ethiopia is the seat of the African Union, the source of the Blue Nile, the homeland of coffee, and proudly home to humanity's oldest known ancestor — Lucy, the 3.2-million-year-old hominid skeleton.

### The Local

**🛍 Shops**

1. **HERITAGE · ✦ COFFEE** — *Tomoca Coffee, Addis Ababa*
   The 1953 Tomoca — the heritage Ethiopian coffee roaster, the country's most famous coffee export.
   *Tags: Family · Business · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The Piazza branch is the heritage 1953 location; the espresso is the architectural booking.

2. **TEXTILES · ✦ HABESHA** — *Sabahar / Muya Ethiopia, Addis Ababa*
   The handwoven cotton ateliers — the heritage *habesha kemis* and *netela* makers.
   *Tags: Romantic · Family*
   > Etiquette tip: Sabahar's Sholla Bole atelier offers tours; the natural-dye work is the heritage.

3. **MARKET · ✦ MERKATO** — *Merkato, Addis Ababa*
   The largest open-air market in Africa — the heritage commerce of the capital.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: Hire a local guide; the recoda (silver) and basket sections are the heritage purchases.

**🍽 Dining**

1. **RESTAURANT · ✦ ETHIOPIAN HERITAGE** — *Yod Abyssinia, Addis Ababa*
   The cultural-restaurant institution — the heritage *injera*-and-dance Ethiopian showcase.
   *Tags: Family · Friendly*
   > Etiquette tip: The traditional dancers from Ethiopia's regions perform throughout dinner; the *beyaynetu* platter is the heritage choice.
